Buyer's Exhaustion Ends Option in Credit Murabahah
Ruling when buyer exhausts item in credit Murabahah with hidden term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a Murabahah buyer exhausts the item after discovering a hidden credit term, and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) based on the nature of the term not being mal mutaqawwim.

Core Idea
Exhaust the item, lose the option — the credit term is not real wealth, so pay full price.

In a Murabahah (cost-plus) sale, if the seller conceals a credit term, the buyer has an option to return the item as long as it is intact. But what if the buyer uses or consumes it before returning? This passage clarifies that once the item is exhausted (consumed or perished), the buyer loses the option and must pay the contracted price. The reasoning hinges on the legal status of time (ajal): it is not considered valuable property (mal mutaqawwim) for the purpose of refund, even though it is treated as wealth for requiring disclosure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two events that make the sale binding
The passage states that if the buyer exhausts the sold item or it perishes by itself, the sale becomes binding (lazim). The buyer can no longer return the item.
Exhausting includes consuming, using up, or destroying the item.
2
Understand the ruling: no option and no recourse
Once the item is gone, the buyer loses the option (khiyar) and cannot recover any part of the price. He must pay the full amount agreed upon.
This is the mufta bihi position: the buyer bears the full cost.
3
Grasp the ta'lil: the credit term is not mal mutaqawwim
The core legal reason (illa) is that the credit term (ajal) is not real property. Therefore, no portion of the price corresponds to it; the price increase is merely for ease (tarafuh).
Mal mutaqawwim is property that can be owned and compensated. Time lacks this quality in reality.
4
Apply the dual role of the term
In Murabahah, the term is treated as wealth for the purpose of requiring disclosure (to avoid cheating) but not for the purpose of allowing a refund after consumption. This explains why the option exists only while the item is extant.
This dual treatment is the key analytical point.
5
Extend the ruling to Tadwil and perishing
The same ruling applies to Tadwil (a similar cost-based sale) and when the item perishes by itself, not just when the buyer consumes it.
The option is conditional on the item's existence in all cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن أتلف أي المشتري المبيع أو تلف بنفسه. لزم إلخ لأن الأجل ليس بمال متقوم، فلا يقابله شيء من الثمن، وإنما فيه ترفه، فيزاد الثمن لأجله، فيثبت له الخيار إذا كان المبيع قائماً نظراً لهذا الجانب، وإذا هلك أو استهلكه المشتري، لم يبق له الخيار نظراً لجانب عدم المالية في الأجل حقيقة، والحاصل: أن للأجل شبهة المقابلة ثابتة؛ لأنه يزاد في الثمن لأجله، فاعتبر الأجل مالاً في المرابحة، حتى اشترط بيان الأجل احترازاً عن شبهة الخيانة، ولم يعتبر في حق الرجوع؛ لأنه ليس بمال في الحقيقة. (كفايه، فتح) ومائة: ولا يرجع بشيء، وكذا الحكم في هلاك المبيع. (ط، عيني) وكذا التولية في جميع ما مر من الخيار ما دام المبيع قائما. (ط، عيني)
And if he exhausts, i.e., the buyer exhausts the sold item or it perishes by itself, it becomes binding, etc., because the term is not a valuable property, so nothing of the price corresponds to it; rather, there is ease in it, so the price is increased because of it. Thus, the option is established for him while the item is extant, considering this aspect. When it perishes or the buyer consumes it, he no longer has the option, considering the aspect of the non-existence of wealth in the term in reality. The sum is: the term has a semblance of consideration because the price is increased for it, so the term is considered a wealth in Murabahah such that disclosure of the term is required to avoid the semblance of cheating. But it is not considered for the purpose of recourse because it is not wealth in reality. And one hundred: he does not recover anything. The same applies if the sold item perishes. Similarly for Tadwil in all the above options as long as the item is extant.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the consequence when the buyer in a Murabahah with a hidden credit term exhausts the item (e.g., consumes it) or it perishes. While the item is still intact, the buyer has the option to return it upon discovering the hidden term. However, if the item is consumed or destroyed, the buyer loses the option and must pay the full price (including the profit) as per the contract. He cannot recover anything from the seller. The reason is that the credit term is not real property (mal muttaqawwim); it is merely a convenience that causes the price to increase. In Murabahah, the term is treated as if it were a form of wealth to require disclosure, but for the purpose of recourse (e.g., demanding a refund), it is not considered wealth. Therefore, if the item is gone, the buyer bears the full cost. The same rule applies to Tadwil.

Key Terms
المال المتقوم (al-mal al-mutaqawwim): Valuable property that can be legally owned and compensated; the credit term lacks this quality in reality.
الأجل (al-ajal): The credit term or deferment period in a sale; a time-based condition that is not tangible property.
التولية (al-tadwil): A sale at cost price (like Murabahah but without profit); the same option rules apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, what is the consequence if the buyer in a Murabahah with a hidden credit term consumes the sold item?
A) The contract becomes void, and the buyer must return the item's value.
B) The buyer keeps the item and pays only the cost price (excluding profit).
C) The buyer loses the option and must pay the full price; he cannot recover anything.
D) The buyer can still return the item and receive a refund of the full price.

Key Takeaway
If the buyer exhausts or the item perishes, the sale becomes binding and the buyer must pay the full price — the credit term is not real wealth.

Tadwil (Assignment Sale) with Unknown Cost Price
Ruling on Tadwil with unknown cost price and intra-Hanafi dispute on remedy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of a Tadwil sale when the cost price is unknown, explain the effect of learning the price in vs. after the session, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the remedy when the item is exhausted.

Core Idea
Ignorance of the cost price voids a Tadwil contract, but knowledge acquired in the session rescues it.

Tadwil is a sale where the seller passes on the item at cost. But what happens if the buyer doesn't know what that cost was? The Hanafi masters lay out a clear ruling: the sale is void due to uncertainty. However, there is nuance: if the buyer learns the price in the same session, the contract becomes valid with an option. And if the item is already used up? An internal dispute arises between Abu Yusuf and the later fatwa. Let's walk through the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The primary ruling: if the buyer does not know the cost price at the time of contract, the sale is fasid (void) due to jahalah (ignorance) causing gharar.
Jahalah al-thaman (ignorance of price) is a fundamental defect.
2
Apply the temporal condition
If the buyer learns the exact cost in the same session (majlis) before separation, the ignorance is removed and the contract becomes valid; the buyer then has an option (khiyar) to accept or reject.
Learning after separation does not cure the defect.
3
Examine the exhausted item scenario
If the buyer exhausts (consumes/destroys) the item before learning the price, the contract cannot be rescinded; instead, the buyer must pay a spot price. The seller does not refund anything.
This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf holds that the buyer returns the market value of the item and recovers the full price paid. The preferred fatwa (Abu Ja'far) values the item at spot and deferred prices and refunds the difference.
The tarjih relies on customary practice (ta'aruf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ولّى رجلاً شيئاً بما قام عليه، ولم يعلم المشتري بكم قام عليه فسد، ولو علم في المجلس خيّر قبل الافتراق. أي إن باع المشتري بالتولية من رجل و لم يبين أن الثمن نسيئة ثم علم المشتري الثاني، رده إن شاء وأخذه بكل الثمن إن شاء، وإن أتلفه ثم علم أن الثمن كان مؤجلا لزمه بثمن حال، ولا يرجع على البائع بشيء، وعند أبي يوسف يرد قيمة العين ويسترد كل الثمن، وقال الفقيه أبو جعفر المختار للفتوى أن يقيم المبيع بثمن حال وبثمن مؤجل، فيرجع المشتري على البائع بفضل ما بينهما للتعارف، والصحيح أنه يفتي بالرد إذا وجد التعزير، وبدونه لا يفتى به رمز الحقائق: ٥٣/٢] (فتح) ومن ولى إلخ: أي إذا قال: "وليتك هذا الشيء بما قام علي يريد به ما اشتراه به مع ما لحقه المؤن كالصبغ والفتل وغير ذلك، والحال أنه لم يعلم المشتري بكم قام على المولي فسد البيع؛ لجهالة الثمن، ولو علم المشتري مبلغ الثمن في المجلس خير بين أخذه وتركه؛ لأن جهالة الثمن فساد في صلب العقد إلا أنه في مجلس العقد غير متقرر، فإذا علم فيه ارتفعت الجهالة، وإنما يتخير بعد العلم في المجلس؛ لأن الرضا بالشيء لا يتم قبل العلم به، ولو علم بعد الافتراق لا ينقلب البيع صحيحا لتقرر الفساد، ولا يجوز إلا بتجديد عقد.
And if someone assigns (yuwalli) a man an item at the price it cost him, and the buyer does not know what it cost him, the sale is void. If he learns in the session, he is given a choice before separation. That is, if the buyer sells by Tadwil to a man and did not disclose that the price was on credit, then the second buyer knows, he may return it if he wishes or take it for the full price if he wishes. If he exhausts it and then learns that the price was deferred, he must pay a spot price and cannot recover anything from the seller. According to Abu Yusuf, he returns the value of the item and recovers all the price. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far said the chosen fatwa is to value the item at spot price and deferred price, then the buyer recovers from the seller the difference between them due to custom. The correct view is that the fatwa is given for return if there is deterrence (ta'zir), otherwise not. And 'man walla' etc.: meaning if he says, 'I assign you this item at what it cost me,' intending what he bought it for along with expenses like dyeing, twisting, etc., and the buyer does not know what cost the assignor, the sale is void due to ignorance of the price. If the buyer learns the amount of the price in the session, he has the choice between taking it or leaving it, because ignorance of the price is a defect in the core of the contract, but it is not settled in the session; if he learns in it, the ignorance is removed, and he only gets the choice after knowledge because satisfaction with something is not complete before knowledge. If he learns after separation, the sale does not become valid due to the confirmation of voidness, and it is not permissible except by renewing the contract.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage discusses the Tadwil (assignment) sale, where the seller says 'I assign this to you at what it cost me.' The cost price must be known to the buyer for the contract to be valid. If the buyer does not know the cost, the sale is void due to ignorance (jahalah) of the price, which is a fundamental defect. However, if the buyer learns the exact cost in the same session (majlis) before they separate, the ignorance is removed and the contract becomes valid; the buyer then has the option to accept or reject. If he learns after the session ends, the contract remains void and cannot be rectified without a new contract. The passage also notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: if the buyer exhausts the item and later learns the original price was on credit, Abu Yusuf says he returns the market value and recovers the full price paid; the preferred fatwa according to Abu Ja'far is to calculate the difference between the spot price and deferred price and refund that difference, customarily. The final note says the fatwa for returning the item (rescission) is given only if there is deterrence (ta'zir), otherwise not.

Key Terms
التولية (al-tawliyah): An assignment sale where the seller sells the item at exactly the same price he paid, without profit.
الجهالة (al-jahalah): Ignorance of a material term (here the price) that renders the contract fasid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The buyer has the option to accept or reject.
D) The seller must reduce the price to the buyer's estimate.

Key Takeaway
A Tadwil sale is void if the cost price is unknown; learning in the session saves it with an option; after session, it remains void and requires a new contract.

Selling Real Estate Before Taking Possession: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on pre-possession sale of real estate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on selling real estate before possession, and explain the dalil and reasoning for each position.

Core Idea
Real estate can be sold before possession because it rarely perishes, unlike movables – an exception to the general hadith.

In this lesson, we examine a classical intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a buyer can sell real estate before taking possession. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) allow it, while Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani forbids it based on a general hadith. We will analyze the proofs and reasoning of each side, and understand why the fatwa follows the view of the two shaykhs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the specific fiqh question? Can a buyer of real estate resell it before taking possession (qabd)?
2
State the Hanafi position (two shaykhs)
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, such a sale is valid (sahih).
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
State the opposing view (Muhammad)
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds it is invalid (ghayr sahih) based on the general hadith.
Ahmad and al-Shafi'i also held this view.
4
Analyze the proofs
Muhammad cites the hadith: 'If you buy something, do not sell it until you take possession of it.' The two shaykhs argue the hadith is particularized (makhsus) to movables due to the risk of destruction; real estate is rarely destroyed. They also cite ijma on disposing of price and dower before possession.
This is a form of takhsis by 'illa and ijma.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon fatwa is the position of the two shaykhs (al-fatwa 'ala qawl al-shaykhayn).
This is the operative ruling in the Hanafi school.

فصل صح بيع العقار قبل قبضه، ... الذي اشتراه عند الشيخين خلافا لمحمد. صح عند الشيخين، وعند محمد : لا يصح؛ لقوله عليه: "إذا اشتريت شيئاً فلا تبعه حتى تقبضه"، رواه أحمد و به قال أحمد والشافعي، ولهما: أن عدم الجواز في المنقول لخطر انفساخ البيع بهلاك المعقود عليه في يد البائع قبل القبض، والهلاك لا يتحقق في العقار غالباً، فإن قيل: إنه تعليل في موضع النص، وهو غير مقبول، أجيب: بأن النص عام دخله الخصوص؛ لإجماعنا على جواز التصرف في الثمن والصداق قبل القبض، ومثل هذا العام يجوز -
Section: The sale of real estate before taking possession is valid according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad. It is valid according to the two shaykhs, but according to Muhammad it is not valid due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'If you buy something, do not sell it until you take possession of it,' narrated by Ahmad, and Ahmad and al-Shafi'i also held this view. Their (the two shaykhs') argument is that the lack of permissibility in movable property is due to the risk of the contract being rescinded by the destruction of the subject matter in the seller's hands before delivery, and destruction is generally not realized in real estate. If it is said: this is an explanation in the place of the text (i.e., against the apparent meaning of the hadith), it is not accepted. The answer is that the text is general but has been particularized; by our consensus on the permissibility of disposing of the price and the dower before taking possession, and such a general text may be -
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of selling real estate before the buyer takes possession of it. According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), it is valid. According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, it is not valid, based on the hadith 'Do not sell what you have not yet taken possession of' (a general prohibition). The two shaykhs argue that the prohibition in the hadith applies primarily to movable goods (manqulat) because they risk being destroyed in the seller's hands before delivery, but real estate ('aqar) rarely perishes. They also point out that the same general hadith has been particularized by consensus: for example, it is permissible to dispose of the price (thaman) and the dower (sadaq) before taking possession. Therefore, the general ruling can be limited.

Key Terms
العقار (al-'aqar): Real estate, immovable property such as land and buildings.
القَبْض (al-qabd): Taking possession/delivery; for real estate, possession is typically by vacating (takhliyah) the premises.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qiyas on movable property.
B) The hadith: 'If you buy something, do not sell it until you take possession of it.'
C) Ijma of the Companions.
D) The principle that gharar invalidates contracts.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the general prohibition of selling before possession is particularized to movables; real estate is an exception due to the lack of risk of destruction.

Tawliyah Sale and Undisclosed Deferred Payment
Ruling on tawliyah when deferred payment is hidden

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of a tawliyah sale when the cost is unknown, explain the session cure, and compare the three Hanafi positions on recourse after the goods are destroyed.

Core Idea
A tawliyah sale is void if the cost is hidden, but knowledge during the session cures it; the deferred term is not property, so recourse is limited.

This passage deals with a specific type of trust-based sale called tawliyah, where the seller says 'I sell this for what it cost me.' If the buyer does not know the actual cost, the sale is corrupt due to ignorance of price. However, the law provides a cure if the buyer learns the cost during the contract session. The passage also explores the legal nature of a deferred payment term and how it affects rights when the goods are destroyed. An intra-Hanafi dispute arises among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Faqih Abu Jafar on the correct recourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Recognize that tawliyah is a sale at cost. If the buyer does not know the cost at contract, the sale becomes fasid (corrupt) due to jahalat al-thaman.
The base text states: '...and the buyer does not know the sale to the buyer... it becomes corrupt.'
2
Locate the session cure
If the buyer learns the cost during the same session (before separation), he has an option to accept or reject. This removes the ignorance and validates the sale.
The cure only works if knowledge is gained in the session. After separation, the fasād is settled and a new contract is needed.
3
Understand the legal nature of ajal (deferred term)
The passage analyzes why a deferred term is not considered real property (māl mutaqawwim). It only has a semblance of correspondence (shubhat al-muqabalah) because the price is increased for it, but it cannot be a basis for financial recourse.
This explains why in murabahah the deferment must be disclosed, but in a tawliyah with hidden deferment, the second buyer cannot reclaim the full price after destruction.
4
Compare the three Hanafi positions on recourse after destruction
Three views exist: (1) Abu Hanifa / Sahibayn: second buyer pays immediate price and reclaims nothing; (2) Abu Yusuf: returns value and reclaims full price; (3) Faqih Abu Jafar: evaluate the item at immediate and deferred market prices, refund the difference.
The muftā bihi (relied-upon fatwa) is Abu Jafar's view, but the fatwa of return is only given if there is a deterrent (taʿzīr) against fraud.

Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on tawliyah (sale at cost price) when the underlying transaction involved deferred payment. The author states that if someone sells an item by tawliyah (i.e., he says 'I sell this to you at what it cost me') and the buyer does not know the exact cost (including expenses like dyeing), the sale is corrupt due to ignorance of the price. However, if the buyer learns the actual cost during the same session (before separation), he has a choice to either accept the sale at that price or reject it. This is because the defect (jahala) is not yet settled during the session; once knowledge is obtained, the ignorance is removed. If he learns after the session ends, the sale remains invalid and requires a new contract. The commentary then discusses a specific case: if the original price was deferred (credit sale) and the seller in tawliyah did not mention this, the second buyer has an option only while the goods exist. If the goods are destroyed or consumed before learning of the deferred nature, the second buyer must pay the immediate price and cannot recover anything from his seller (the first buyer). The author notes a difference from Abu Yusuf, who holds that the buyer returns the value of the item and reclaims the full price paid. The preferred fatwa according to Faqih Abu Jafar is to evaluate the item at its immediate and deferred market prices and have the first buyer refund the difference. In practice, the fatwa of return is only given if there is a deterrent (ta'zir) against fraudulent behavior; otherwise, it is not applied. The fundamental principle is that a deferred term (ajal) is not real property in itself, but it has a semblance of value because prices are increased for it. This affects the rulings: in murabahah (cost-plus sale), disclosure of the term is required to avoid treachery, but in cases of recourse (e.g., when the item is destroyed), the term is not considered wealth so no compensation is due. The overall ruling is that the tawliyah sale is invalid if the buyer does not know the cost at the time of contract, but if he learns during the session, the sale becomes valid with a choice; after separation, it remains invalid.

Key Terms
التولية (al-tawliyah): A sale at cost price where the seller says 'I sell this to you for what it cost me'.
أجل (ajal): A deferred term for payment in a credit sale.
جهالة الثمن (jahalat al-thaman): Ignorance of the price in a contract, which renders the sale corrupt (fasid) until resolved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The seller must refund the full price.

Key Takeaway
A tawliyah sale is fasid if the cost is unknown, but session knowledge cures it; the deferred term is not property, so recourse after destruction is limited to market value difference under the muftā bihi.

Selling Real Estate Before Possession: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on selling real estate before possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the two shaykhs permit selling real estate before possession and state the mufta bihi for leasing.

Core Idea
Real estate is not subject to destruction, so selling before possession is valid — but leasing is treated like movables.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi disagreement: may a buyer resell real estate before taking physical delivery? The two shaykhs and Muhammad differ, and the dispute reveals how the school uses analogy (qiyas) to specify a general hadith. We will trace the arguments and see how the later school harmonized them for sale and leasing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act in question is the buyer selling the purchased real estate before taking physical possession (qabd). The dispute is whether this is valid.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi between the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that selling real estate before possession is valid. Muhammad holds it is invalid. External schools (Ahmad, al-Shafi'i) agree with Muhammad.
The two shaykhs' view is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the basis for fatwa on sale.
3
Analyze the proofs
Muhammad cites the Prophet's general hadith: 'If you buy something, do not sell it until you take possession of it.' The two shaykhs respond that the hadith is specific to movable property because the prohibition is based on risk of destruction, which does not apply to real estate. They support this by noting consensus on the permissibility of transacting in price and dowry before possession.
The two shaykhs use qiyas (analogy) to specify the general text, which is acceptable in Hanafi usul.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: under the two shaykhs, a buyer can resell real estate before taking keys; under Muhammad, he cannot. The mufta bihi for sale follows the two shaykhs. For leasing before possession, the correct view (sahh) is that it is invalid by agreement, and the fatwa is upon that.
Leasing is treated as invalid for both because benefits are like movables in potential destruction.

فصل: في التصرف في المبيع والثمن قبل القبض والزيادة والحط فيهما وتأجيل المديون. (ط) صح عند الشيخين، وعند محمد : لا يصح؛ لقوله عليه: "إذا اشتريت شيئاً فلا تبعه حتى تقبضه"، رواه أحمد و به قال أحمد والشافعي، ولهما: أن عدم الجواز في المنقول لخطر انفساخ البيع بهلاك المعقود عليه في يد البائع قبل القبض، والهلاك لا يتحقق في العقار غالباً، فإن قيل: إنه تعليل في موضع النص، وهو غير مقبول، أجيب: بأن النص عام دخله الخصوص؛ لإجماعنا على جواز التصرف في الثمن والصداق قبل القبض، ومثل هذا العام يجوز تخصيصه بالقياس فحملناه على المنقول حتى لو تصور هلاك العقار لا يجوز بيعه قبل قبضه بأن كان على شط نهر، وما رواه معلول بغرر انفساخ العقد بالهلاك قبل القبض، والإجارة قبل القبض على هذا الخلاف. ولا يجوز للمشتري أن يؤاجر الدار المشتراة قبل القبض عند محمد، وعندهما يجوز والأصح أن الإجارة لا تصح اتفاقا وعليه الفتوى؛ لأن الإجارة تمليك المنافع، والمنافع كالمنقول في احتمال الهلاك، وكذا لا يجوز بالاتفاق بيع والعقار الذي لا يؤمن أن تغلب عليه الرمال. (عيني، فتح، كفاية) لا بيع المنقول: قبل قبضه سواء كان طعاما أو غيره. (ط)]
Section: On transacting in the sold item and price before possession, and the increase and decrease in them, and postponing a debt (for the debtor). (T) It is valid according to the two shaykhs, and according to Muhammad: it is not valid; due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'If you buy something, do not sell it until you take possession of it,' narrated by Ahmad, and Ahmad and al-Shafi'i adopted this. And for them (the two shaykhs): that the impermissibility in movable property is due to the risk of the contract being rescinded by the destruction of the subject matter in the seller's hand before possession, and destruction is not usually realized in real estate. If it is said: This is a rationalization in the place of the text, and it is unacceptable, the answer is: that the text is general but includes specificity; because of our consensus on the permissibility of transacting in the price and dowry before possession, and such a general text can be specified by analogy, so we apply it to movable property. Even if destruction of real estate is conceivable, its sale before possession is not allowed, such as if it is on a riverbank. And what he narrated is defective due to the uncertainty (gharar) of the contract being rescinded by destruction before possession. And leasing before possession follows this disagreement. It is not permissible for the buyer to lease the purchased house before possession according to Muhammad, and according to the two shaykhs it is permissible. The correct view is that leasing is not valid by agreement, and the fatwa is upon that; because leasing is the transfer of benefits, and benefits are like movable property in the potential of destruction. Likewise, it is not permissible by consensus to sell real estate that is not safe from being overwhelmed by sand. (Ayni, Fath, Kifayah) No sale of movable property before possession, whether it is food or other. (T)
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether real estate can be sold before the buyer has taken physical possession (qabd). The author sets out the section on transacting in the sold item and price before possession. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that it is valid to sell real estate before possession, while Muhammad al-Shaybani holds it is not valid. Muhammad's evidence is the Prophet's hadith: 'If you buy something, do not sell it until you take possession of it.' The two shaykhs argue that the prohibition applies to movable property because there is a risk of the contract being rescinded if the item is destroyed in the seller's hands before possession, and real estate is generally not subject to such destruction. They claim that the hadith is general but can be specified by analogy (qiyas) because there is consensus on the permissibility of transacting in the price (thaman) and dower (mahr) before possession. Therefore, the hadith is applied specifically to movable property. If it were possible for real estate to be destroyed (e.g., a house on a riverbank), then even according to the two shaykhs, its sale before possession would not be allowed. The passage then discusses leasing (ijarah) before possession: Muhammad prohibits it, while the two shaykhs allow it. However, the author notes that the correct view (al-sahh) is that leasing is not valid by agreement (ittifaqan), and the fatwa is upon that, because leasing transfers benefits and benefits are like movable property in the potential of destruction. This shows a practical harmonization. Finally, it states that it is also impermissible by consensus to sell real estate that is not safe from being covered by sand (i.e., subject to destruction). The passage concludes: 'No sale of movable property before possession, whether food or other.'

Key Terms
الشيخان (al-shaykhan): In this context, refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two senior scholars of the school).
قبض (qabd): Physical possession or taking delivery of the purchased item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), why is selling real estate before possession permitted?
A) Because the hadith on this issue is weak.
B) Because real estate is not subject to destruction that would rescind the contract.
C) Because real estate is not considered property.
D) Because the buyer already gained ownership at the time of contract.

Key Takeaway
The two shaykhs permit selling real estate before possession due to absence of destruction risk, but leasing before possession is invalid by agreement.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Selling Movables Before Possession and Re-Measuring Goods
Ruling on selling before possession and conditions for re-measurement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling movable property before possession and explain the obligation to re-measure measured goods when reselling by measure.

Core Idea
Selling movables before possession is invalid; re-measurement is required when reselling measured goods by measure to verify ownership of potential excess.

This lesson addresses two key sales rules: the general prohibition on selling movable property before possession, and the specific requirement to re-measure goods when reselling by measure. Understanding these rules protects both buyer and seller from invalid transactions and ensures that any excess quantity is properly returned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on movable property before possession
State that sale of any movable (manqul) before possession is invalid (fasid). Note that other transactions like gift, charity, loan are allowed according to Imam Muhammad (the most correct view), but not according to Abu Yusuf. Also note the cross-madhhab difference: Malik and Ahmad allow sale of non-food movables before possession.
The prohibition is based on the hadith 'Do not sell what you do not possess.'
2
Distinguish between four scenarios of re-measurement
When a person buys measured goods (makil) and wants to resell, there are four cases: (1) buy by measure, sell by measure – requires re-measurement; (2) buy by estimate, sell by estimate – no re-measurement needed; (3) buy by measure, sell by estimate – no re-measurement needed; (4) buy by estimate, sell by measure – no re-measurement needed for the second buyer.
Re-measurement is only required when both the original purchase and the resale are by measure.
3
Apply the hadith of Jabir as the proof
The hadith states: 'The Prophet prohibited the sale of food until two measures pass: the measure of the seller and the measure of the buyer.' This shows that when buying and selling by measure, the buyer must re-measure before reselling to avoid selling any potential excess that belongs to the first seller.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but acted upon by the Hanafi school.
4
Determine the consequence of eating before re-measurement
If a buyer eats some of the measured food before re-measuring, it is sinful (ithm) because he neglected the command to measure, but the food itself is not unlawful (not haram) because he owns it. He must, however, compensate if a deficit is found.
The sin is in abandoning the wajib (measurement), not in consuming one's own property.
5
Extend the ruling to weighed items
The same illa (reason) applies to weighed goods (mawzun): any excess beyond the original weight belongs to the seller, so re-weighing is required before resale by weight. This extension is by qiyas, as mentioned in the text.
The rule applies to both makil (measured) and mawzun (weighed) goods.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا بيع المنقول: قبل قبضه سواء كان طعاما أو غيره. (ط)] أي لا يصح بيع المنقول قبل القبض؛ لأنه عليها نهى عن بيع ما لم يقبض، وعند مالك بيع الطعام بالطعام قبل القبض لا يجوز، وبيع ما سواه من المنقولات يجوز قبل القبض، وبه قال أحمد، وقيد بالبيع؛ لأنه لو وهب أو تصدق به أو أقرضه أو رهنه أو أعاره من غير البائع لم يجز عند أبي يوسف، ويجوز عند محمد، وهو الأصح، وما لا يجوز بيعه قبل القبض لا يجوز إجارته، ولو أوصى لرجل قبل القبض، صحت الوصية بالإجماع؛ لأن الوصية أخت الميراث، والميراث يصح قبل القبض فكذا الوصية. وفي "الإيضاح " : كل عوض يملك بالعقد، ينفسخ العقد فيه بهلاكه قبل القبض، ولم يجز التصرف فيه كالمبيع والأجرة إذا كانت ميتاً، وبدل الصلح إذا كان معيناً، وما لا ينفسخ العقد فيه بهلاكه، فالتصرف فيه جائز قبل القبض كالمهر، وبدل الخلع، والعتق على مال، وبدل الصلح عن دم العمد رمز الحقائق: ٥٤/٢] (فتح) ولو اشترى مكيلاً إلخ [ أي من حيث شرط المكيل] أي لو اشترى المكيل وأراد أن يتصرف فيه فذلك على أربعة أقسام اشترى مكايلة وباع مكايلة، أو اشترى مجازفة وباع كذلك أو اشترى مكايلة وباع المشتري مجازفة، أو بالعكس من ذلك، ففي الأول لم يجز للمشتري من الأول أن يبيعه حتى يعيد الكيل لنفسه كما كان الحكم في حق المشتري الأول كذلك؛ لما روى جابر الله : " أنه عليها نهى عن بيع الطعام حتى يجري فيه صاعان: صاع البائع وصاع المشتري"، رواه ابن ماجه والدار قطني؛ ولأنه إن زاد على المشروط وذلك للبائع، والتصرف في مال الغير حرام فيجب التحرز عنه وهذه العلة موجودة في الموزون فكان مثله. وفي الثاني لا يحتاج إلى الكيل لعدم الافتقار إلى تعين المقدار، وفي القسمين الأخيرين لا يحتاج المشتري الثاني إلى الكيل؛ لأنه لما اشترى مجازفة ملك جميع ما كان مشاراً إليه فكان متصرفا في ملك نفسه؛ ولأن الزيادة له إذا وجده أكثر من كيل البائع، وكذا لو باع الثوب مذارعة ولم يسم لكل ذراع ثمناً؛ لأن الزيادة له على ما مر. وأكله وكذا كل تصرف يبني على الملك كالهبة والوصية ولا يلزم من حرمة أكله قبل إعادة الكيل كون الطعام حراما، حتى لو أكله وقبضه بلا كيل لا يقال: إنه أكل حراما؛ لأنه أكل ملك نفسه إلا أنه أثم لتركه ما أمر به من الكيل. (عيني، فتح، عناية)
No sale of movable property: before its possession, whether it is food or otherwise. (T) Meaning, the sale of movable property before possession is not valid; because they (the scholars) prohibited the sale of what has not been taken possession of. According to Malik, the sale of food for food before possession is not allowed, but the sale of other movable property before possession is allowed, and Ahmad said likewise. And it is restricted to sale; because if he gives as a gift, charity, loan, pawn, or lends for use to someone other than the seller, it is not allowed according to Abu Yusuf, but it is allowed according to Muhammad, and that is the most correct. And what is not allowed to be sold before possession is not allowed to be leased. If he makes a will for a man before possession, the will is valid by consensus; because the will is the sibling of inheritance, and inheritance is valid before possession, so likewise the will. In al-Idah: Every consideration that is owned by contract, the contract is rescinded upon its destruction before possession, and transacting in it is not allowed, like the sold item and the rent if it is a dead thing, and the substitute of sulh if it is specific. And what the contract is not rescinded by its destruction, transacting in it is allowed before possession, like the mahr, substitute of khul', emancipation for money, and substitute of sulh for intentional homicide. (Rumuz al-Haqaiq: 2/54) (Fath) And if he buys a measured (makil) item, etc. [i.e., regarding the condition of the measured item] i.e., if he buys a measured item and wants to transact in it, that falls into four categories: he buys by measure and sells by measure; or he buys by estimate (mujazafah) and sells likewise; or he buys by measure and sells by estimate; or the opposite of that. In the first, it is not permissible for the first buyer to sell it until he re-measures for himself, just as the ruling was in the right of the first buyer similarly; due to what Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) narrated: 'He (peace be upon him) forbade the sale of food until two measures are passed: the measure of the seller and the measure of the buyer,' narrated by Ibn Majah and al-Daraqutni; and because if it increases beyond what was stipulated, that belongs to the seller, and transacting in the property of another is prohibited, so one must be cautious, and this illa is present in weighed items, so they are similar. In the second, he does not need to measure due to lack of need to determine the amount. In the last two types, the second buyer does not need to measure, because when he bought by estimate, he owned all that was pointed to, so he is transacting in his own property; and because the increase belongs to him if he finds it more than the seller's measure. Likewise, if he sells a cloth by cubit without specifying a price for each cubit, because the increase is his as mentioned. And eating it, and likewise every transaction based on ownership like gift and will, and the prohibition of eating it before repeating the measure does not mean the food is unlawful, such that if he eats it and takes possession without measuring, it is not said that he ate unlawful; because he ate his own property, except that he sinned by abandoning what he was commanded regarding measure. (Ayni, Fath, Inayah)
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This lesson covers two distinct but related rulings: (1) the sale of movable property before possession, and (2) the requirement of re-measurement when reselling measured goods. The author first states the general principle: movables cannot be sold before possession, whether food or other items. The commentary notes that according to Imam Malik and Ahmad ibn Hanbal, non-food movables may be sold before possession, but the Hanafi position is that all movables are included. The prohibition applies only to sale; other transactions like gift, charity, loan, pawn, or lending for use are allowed according to Muhammad (and this is the correct view), but not according to Abu Yusuf. The same prohibition applies to leasing. However, a will is valid by consensus because it is analogous to inheritance. The passage then cites al-Idah which provides a general principle: if a contract is rescinded by destruction of the subject matter before possession (like sale of specific goods), then transacting in it before possession is not allowed. If the contract is not rescinded by destruction (like dower, khul', etc.), then transacting is allowed. The second part discusses the resale of measured goods (makil) by the second buyer. The author divides cases into four based on whether the original purchase and resale are by measure (mukayalah) or by estimate (mujazafah). The first case (buy by measure, sell by measure) requires the second buyer to re-measure the goods before reselling, due to the hadith of Jabir that the Prophet forbade selling food until two measures (that of the seller and the buyer) pass. The reason is that any excess beyond the original measure belongs to the first seller, and the buyer cannot sell what he does not own. This rule also applies to weighed items. In the second case (buy by estimate, sell by estimate), no re-measurement is needed because there is no specific quantity to verify. In the last two mixed cases (buy by measure, sell by estimate or vice versa), the second buyer does not need to re-measure because he owns the entire item by estimate. The same applies to cloth sold by cubit without naming a price per cubit. Finally, the author clarifies that eating the food before re-measurement, though sinful (due to disobeying the command to measure), is not unlawful because the food is his own property. He sins by abandoning the obligation to measure, but the act of eating itself is not haram.

Key Terms
منقول (manqul): Movable property; anything that can be physically transferred.
مكيل (makil): Goods that are sold by measure (volume), such as grains.
مجازفة (mujazafah): Sale by estimate or lump sum without specifying exact measure or weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He can sell immediately because he already measured once.
B) He must re-measure the goods before selling.
C) He must sell by estimate to avoid measurement issues.
D) He can only sell to the original seller.

Key Takeaway
Selling movables before possession is invalid, and re-measurement is wajib when reselling measured goods by measure to avoid selling what you do not own.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Prohibition of Selling Movable Property Before Possession
General prohibition with inter-madhhab dispute and sub-rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling movable property before possession, distinguish it from Maliki/Hanbali views, apply the ruling to sub-rulings (gift, lease, bequest), and identify the epistemological basis (hadith).

Core Idea
The sale of any movable before possession is invalid in Hanafi school due to the general prophetic prohibition.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses the prohibition of selling movable property before possession (qabd). It states the general rule, cites the hadith, and expands into inter-madhhab differences and sub-rulings regarding leases, gifts, and bequests. Understanding this clarifies when ownership transfers and when it does not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
The text states that the sale of movable property before possession is not valid. Identify which items are included and the basis for the ruling.
The rule is general: all movables, food and non-food.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith 'نهى عن بيع ما لم يقبض'. Note its transmission and interpretation in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is ahad and zanni; the prohibition is interpreted as affecting validity.
3
Compare with Maliki/Hanbali views
Malik and Ahmad permit non-food movables before possession. Understand their basis: they restrict the hadith to food.
Hanafi response: the hadith is general, and the illa of gharar applies to all movables.
4
Expand to sub-rulings
The passage extends the ruling to lease (analogous to sale) and mentions differences in gift, charity, etc. between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
The more correct view (Muhammad) permits gift/charity to non-seller before possession.
5
Categorize considerations
The text distinguishes considerations that, if destroyed before possession, rescind the contract (e.g., specific sold item) from those that do not (e.g., dower, khul').
Bequest is an exception: valid by consensus because akin to inheritance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيوع ما يصح بيعه لا بيع المنقول، ولو اشترى مكيلا حرم بيعه وأكله، أي ما يكال أي كره تحريما للمشتري تخصيصه بالقياس فحملناه على المنقول حتى لو تصور هلاك العقار لا يجوز بيعه قبل قبضه بأن كان على شط نهر، وما رواه معلول بغرر انفساخ العقد بالهلاك قبل القبض، والإجارة قبل القبض على هذا الخلاف. ولا يجوز للمشتري أن يؤاجر الدار المشتراة قبل القبض عند محمد، وعندهما يجوز والأصح أن الإجارة لا تصح اتفاقا العلوعليه الفتوى؛ لأن الإجارة تمليك المنافع، والمنافع كالمنقول في احتمال الهلاك، وكذا لا يجوز بالاتفاق بيع والعقار الذي لا يؤمن أن تغلب عليه الرمال. (عيني، فتح، كفاية) لا بيع المنقول: قبل قبضه سواء كان طعاما أو غيره. (ط)] أي لا يصح بيع المنقول قبل القبض؛ لأنه عليها نهى عن بيع ما لم يقبض، وعند مالك بيع الطعام بالطعام قبل القبض لا يجوز، وبيع ما سواه من المنقولات يجوز قبل القبض، وبه قال أحمد، وقيد بالبيع؛ لأنه لو وهب أو تصدق به أو أقرضه أو رهنه أو أعاره من غير البائع لم يجز عند أبي يوسف، ويجوز عند محمد، وهو الأصح، وما لا يجوز بيعه قبل القبض لا يجوز إجارته، ولو أوصى لرجل قبل القبض، صحت الوصية بالإجماع؛ لأن الوصية أخت الميراث، والميراث يصح قبل القبض فكذا الوصية. وفي "الإيضاح " : كل عوض يملك بالعقد، ينفسخ العقد فيه بهلاكه قبل القبض، ولم يجز التصرف فيه كالمبيع والأجرة إذا كانت ميتاً، وبدل الصلح إذا كان معيناً، وما لا ينفسخ العقد فيه بهلاكه، فالتصرف فيه جائز قبل القبض كالمهر، وبدل الخلع، والعتق على مال، وبدل الصلح عن دم العمد رمز الحقائق: ٥٤/٢] (فتح)
The Book of Sales: What is valid to sell. The sale of movable property [before possession] is not valid. If one buys a measured item, its sale and consumption are prohibited for the buyer. [Commentary:] i.e., what is measured, it is prohibitively disliked for the buyer to specify it by analogy, so we interpret it as movable property, even if destruction of real estate is conceivable, its sale before possession is not valid, as when it is on a riverbank. And what is narrated is defective due to the uncertainty of contract rescission by destruction before possession. And leasing before possession is subject to this difference. The buyer may not lease the purchased house before possession according to Muhammad, but according to the two it is permissible, and the correct view is that leasing is not valid by consensus, and the fatwa is upon that; because leasing is a transfer of benefits, and benefits are like movable property in their susceptibility to destruction. Likewise, by consensus, the sale of real estate that is not safe from being covered by sand is not valid. (Ayni, Fath, Kifaya) [Another note:] The sale of movable property before its possession, whether food or otherwise, is not valid. [i.e.,] The sale of movable property before possession is not valid because the Prophet prohibited selling what one has not taken possession of. According to Malik, the sale of food before possession is not valid, but the sale of other movable property before possession is valid, and Ahmad said the same. He restricted it to sale; for if one gifts, gives in charity, lends, pawns, or lends for use to someone other than the seller, it is not valid according to Abu Yusuf, but it is valid according to Muhammad, and this is the more correct view. And what may not be sold before possession may not be leased. If one makes a bequest to a man before possession, the bequest is valid by consensus because the will is akin to inheritance, and inheritance is valid before possession, so too the will. In al-Idah: Every consideration owned by the contract, the contract is rescinded by its destruction before possession, and disposal thereof is not valid, like the sold item, the rent if it is a specific item, and the substitute for a settlement if specific. And what is not rescinded by destruction, disposal thereof before possession is valid, like the dower, the substitute for khul', manumission for a consideration, and the substitute for settling intentional homicide. (Rumuz al-Haqaiq 54/2) (Fath)
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage states the general prohibition of selling movable property before physical possession, citing the prophetic hadith. The Hanafi position is that the sale of any movable item (whether food or otherwise) before possession is invalid. This is contrasted with the Maliki and Hanbali positions: Malik permits sale of non-food movables before possession, and Ahmad agrees. The prohibition applies specifically to sale; other transactions like gift, charity, loan, pawn, or loan-for-use to a non-seller are invalid according to Abu Yusuf but valid according to Muhammad (the relied-upon view). Leasing before possession follows the same ruling as sale. A significant exception is bequest: a bequest of movable property before possession is valid by consensus because it is akin to inheritance. The passage also categorizes considerations: if the consideration is a specific item that could be destroyed, the contract is rescinded by its destruction before possession; but if it is a debt or non-specific, disposal is allowed before possession (e.g., dower, khul' substitute). This distinction is crucial for understanding the scope of the prohibition.

Key Terms
المنقول (al-manqul): Movable property; anything that can be moved or transported, as opposed to real estate.
القبض (al-qabd): Physical possession or taking delivery; the act of taking control of the purchased item.
الإجارة (al-ijarah): Leasing; a contract for the transfer of usufruct (benefits) in exchange for rent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on selling a piece of furniture (movable) before the buyer takes physical possession?
A) Valid, because furniture is not food

C) Valid only if the price is paid immediately
D) Invalid only if the item is perishable

Key Takeaway
The sale of any movable before possession is invalid in Hanafi school due to the general prophetic prohibition and the underlying cause of uncertainty.

The Obligation of Re-measurement Before Disposal of Purchased Goods
Detailed conditions for re-measuring purchased items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of purchasing measured items and apply the rule of re-measurement for each category, including exceptions.

Core Idea
Re-measurement is wajib before disposal; omitting it is sinful but the item remains permissible.

When you buy a measured item like grain, do you have to measure it again before selling or eating it? The answer depends on how you bought and sold it. This lesson unpacks four scenarios, the hadith that mandates two measures, and important exceptions like hand-to-hand sales and currency. You will also learn the Hanafi position on counted items and a key intra-madhhab difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four scenarios
The passage classifies purchases into four types: (1) bought by measure, sold by measure; (2) bought by guess, sold by guess; (3) bought by measure, sold by guess; (4) bought by guess, sold by measure. Recognise which scenario triggers the re-measurement obligation.
Only scenario 1 (both by measure) requires re-measurement by the buyer.
2
Understand the dalil
The hadith of Jabir (narrated by Ibn Majah and al-Daraqutni) prohibits selling food until two measures have passed: the seller's measure and the buyer's measure. This is the primary evidence.
The hadith is ahad, so it establishes wujub (obligation) in Hanafi usul.
3
Apply the cause (illa) to weighed and counted
The reason (illa) is that any increase over the seller's measure belongs to the seller, and disposing of it without knowing the exact quantity risks consuming another's property. This cause exists for weighed and counted items too, so they are included.
Abu Hanifa includes counted items; the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) exclude them, analogising to items sold by length.
4
Recognise exceptions
No re-measurement is needed in: guess sales (juzaf), hand-to-hand sales (ta'ati), currency (dirhams/dinars), and when the seller measures in the buyer's presence after the sale (one measure suffices).
The fatwa is upon these exceptions.
5
Evaluate the consequence of omission
If a buyer sells or eats without re-measuring, the act is valid but sinful. The food is not forbidden because it is his own property – the sin is for abandoning the command to measure.
This clarifies a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اشترى مكيلا إلخ [ أي من حيث شرط المكيل] أي لو اشترى المكيل وأراد أن يتصرف فيه فذلك على أربعة أقسام اشترى مكايلة وباع مكايلة، أو اشترى مجازفة وباع كذلك أو اشترى مكايلة وباع المشتري مجازفة، أو بالعكس من ذلك، ففي الأول لم يجز للمشتري من الأول أن يبيعه حتى يعيد الكيل لنفسه كما كان الحكم في حق المشتري الأول كذلك؛ لما روى جابر الله : " أنه عليها نهى عن بيع الطعام حتى يجري فيه صاعان: صاع البائع وصاع المشتري"، رواه ابن ماجه والدار قطني؛ ولأنه إن زاد على المشروط وذلك للبائع، والتصرف في مال الغير حرام فيجب التحرز عنه وهذه العلة موجودة في الموزون فكان مثله. وفي الثاني لا يحتاج إلى الكيل لعدم الافتقار إلى تعين المقدار، وفي القسمين الأخيرين لا يحتاج المشتري الثاني إلى الكيل؛ لأنه لما اشترى مجازفة ملك جميع ما كان مشاراً إليه فكان متصرفا في ملك نفسه؛ ولأن الزيادة له إذا وجده أكثر من كيل البائع، وكذا لو باع الثوب مذارعة ولم يسم لكل ذراع ثمناً؛ لأن الزيادة له على ما مر. وأكله وكذا كل تصرف يبني على الملك كالهبة والوصية ولا يلزم من حرمة أكله قبل إعادة الكيل كون الطعام حراما، حتى لو أكله وقبضه بلا كيل لا يقال: إنه أكل حراما؛ لأنه أكل ملك نفسه إلا أنه أثم لتركه ما أمر به من الكيل. (عيني، فتح، عناية) وحتى يكيله، ومثله: الموزون والمعدود، لا المذرُوع، وصح التصرف في الثمن قبل أي حتى يعيد المشتري الكيل قبضه والزيادة فيه. الثمن الموزون إلخ: لا يجوز للمشتري أن يبيع الموزون والمعدود، أو يأكل منهما حتى يعيد الوزن والعدد، وهو مقيد بغير بيع التعاطي، أما إذا كان البيع بالتعاطي، فلا يحتاج إلى إعادة الوزن ثانياً؛ لأنه صار بيعاً بالقبض بعد الوزن، وعليه الفتوى، ومقيد أيضاً بغير الدراهم والدنانير، فيجوز التصرف فيهما بعد القبض قبل الوزن. وفي "المحيط": لو كان المكيل والموزون ثمنا يجوز التصرف فيه قبل الكيل والوزن ولو كاله البائع بحضرة المشتري بعد البيع قبل القبض، قيل: لا يكتفي به؛ لظاهر الحديث، فإنه اشترط فيه صاعين والصحيح أنه يكتفي به؛ لأن المبيع صار معلوماً بكيل واحد، وتحقق معنى التسليم، والحديث محمول على ما إذا اجتمعت الصفقتان على ما نبينه في باب السلم، وجعل المصنف المعدود كالمكيل والموزون، وهو مروي عن أبي حنيفة، وعنه: أنه كالمذروع، وهو قول الصاحبين.
And if one buys a measured item, etc. [i.e., from where the condition of the measured item] i.e., if one buys the measured item and wishes to dispose of it, there are four categories: bought by measure and sells by measure, or bought by guess and sells by guess, or bought by measure and the buyer sells by guess, or vice versa. In the first, it is not permissible for the first buyer to sell it until he re-measures for himself, just as was the ruling regarding the first buyer. This is because of what Jabir narrated: 'The Prophet prohibited the sale of food until two measures have passed: the measure of the seller and the measure of the buyer.' This was narrated by Ibn Majah and al-Daraqutni. And because if there is an increase over the stipulated [measure], it belongs to the seller, and disposing of another's property is forbidden, so one must guard against it. This cause is also present in weighed items, so they are similar. In the second, re-measurement is not needed because there is no need to determine the quantity. In the last two categories, the second buyer does not need re-measurement because when he bought by guess, he owned all that was pointed to, so he is disposing of his own property. And because the increase, if he finds it more than the seller's measure, belongs to him. Similarly, if one sells cloth by the cubit without specifying a price for each cubit, because the increase belongs to him as previously mentioned. And eating it, and likewise any disposal based on ownership like gift and bequest. The prohibition of eating it before re-measurement does not make the food itself forbidden; if he eats it without measuring, he has not eaten something forbidden because he ate his own property, but he sins for abandoning what he was commanded to do: measuring. (Ayni, Fath, Inayah) Until he measures it. Similarly, weighed and counted items [are like measured], not measured by length. And disposal of the price before its possession and the increase in it are valid. Weighed etc.: The buyer may not sell weighed or counted items nor eat from them until he re-weighs or re-counts. This is restricted to non-hand-to-hand sales. As for hand-to-hand sales, there is no need for a second weigh, because it becomes a sale by possession after weighing, and the fatwa is upon this. Also restricted to dirhams and dinars, so disposal of them after possession before weighing is valid. In al-Muhit: If the measured or weighed item is the price, it is permissible to dispose of it before measuring/weighing. And if the seller measures in the presence of the buyer after the sale before possession, it is said: it is not sufficient due to the apparent hadith, for it requires two measures, but the correct opinion is that it is sufficient because the sold item becomes known by one measure, and the meaning of delivery is realized; the hadith is interpreted as when both transactions are combined, as we will explain in the chapter of salam. The author considered counted items like measured and weighed; this is narrated from Abu Hanifa, but there is also a narration that it is like measured by length, which is the view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage details the requirements when a buyer purchases a measured item (e.g., grain) and wishes to resell or consume it. The rule is that the buyer must remeasure the item before any disposal, except in certain cases. The text outlines four scenarios: (1) both purchase and sale by measure: the buyer must remeasure; (2) both by guess (juzaf): no need to remeasure; (3) purchase by measure and sale by guess: no need to remeasure because the buyer owns all that was pointed to; (4) the reverse: also no need. The proof is the hadith of Jabir requiring two measures (seller's and buyer's). The same rule applies to weighed and counted items, except in hand-to-hand sales (ta'ati) where weighing at the time of purchase suffices, and for currency (dirhams/dinars) which can be disposed of before weighing. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa considers counted items like measured/weighed, while the two companions consider them like items sold by length (no requirement). The relied-upon view (fatwa) is that counted items require recounting, but this is subject to the exceptions. The passage also notes that if the seller measures in the buyer's presence after purchase, it is sufficient according to the correct opinion, contrary to a minority view that insists on two separate measures.

Key Terms
مكيل (makil): An item that is measured by volume (e.g., grain, dates).
مجازفة (mujazafah): Sale by guess or lump sum without precise measurement; the price is fixed for the whole lot.
بيع التعاطي (bay' al-ta'ati): A hand-to-hand transaction where the buyer takes the item immediately after weighing/measuring; no formal offer and acceptance necessary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person buys a sack of rice by measure (mikyal) from the seller and then sells it to another person also by measure, what must the first buyer do before selling?
A) Nothing, because the rice was already measured by the seller
B) Re-measure the rice for himself
C) Estimate the amount by guess
D) Seek permission from the original seller

Key Takeaway
A buyer of measured, weighed, or counted items must re-measure before disposal, except in guess sales, hand-to-hand sales, and currency transactions.

Ruling on Items Sold by Length
Ruling on items sold by length and disposal after possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on disposing of an item sold by length after possession and identify the exception when a per-unit price is named.

Core Idea
An item sold by length is fully owned after possession without need to remeasure — unless a price per unit was specified.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq clarifies the Hanafi view on items sold by length (e.g., cloth by the cubit). Unlike items sold by measure (kayl) or weight (wazn), length does not require re-measurement after possession because it is a description, not a quantity. However, the rule changes if a price per unit was stipulated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is disposing of the item sold by length (al-madhru‘) after taking possession. The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) even without re-measuring.
This is a departure from items sold by measure or weight, where possession is incomplete until measurement.
2
Understand the rationale
Length measurement (dhara‘) is a description (wasf) of the item, not a quantity (qadr). Therefore, the entire item belongs to the buyer upon possession, and no adjustment of price is needed if found more or less.
The buyer bears the risk of deficiency unless a per-unit price was named.
3
Spot the exception
If the parties specified a price per unit (e.g., per cubit), then the buyer must measure before disposing of the item. If a deficiency is found, the buyer has an option (khiyar) to reject or accept with price reduction.
The exception protects the buyer from paying for undelivered quantity.
4
Note the legal consequence
If no per-unit price was named, the buyer owns the item absolutely after possession, and any excess or deficiency belongs to the buyer without affecting the price.
This rule is specific to items sold by length; other measurements follow different rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا المذروع: أي لا يحرم التصرف في المبيع المذروع بعد القبض قبل الذرع وإن اشتراه بشرط الذرع؛ لأن الذرع وصف له، وليس بقدر، فيكون كله للمشتري بلا زيادة ثمن ولا نقصان إن وجده زائداً أو ناقصاً، هذا إذا لم لكل ذراع ثمنا، وإن سمى فـ فلا يحل له التصرف فيه حتى يذرع، وفي النقصان يثبت له الخيار. (عيني، فتح) وصح التصرف [ أي تصرف البائع في ثمن المبيع. (عيني)] قبل قبضه سواء كان مما لا يتعين كالنقود أو مما يتعين كالمكيل والموزون، حتى لو باع إبلاً بدراهم أو بكر من الحنطة جاز أن يأخذ بدله شيئاً آخر؛ لحديث ابن عمر ما: "كنا نبيع الإبل بالبقيع فنأخذ مكان الدراهم الدنانير، ومكان الدنانير الدراهم، وكان يجوزه رسول الله "، ولأن النهي ورد في المبيع؛ لاحتمال غرر الانفساخ ولا يتصور ذلك في الثمن؛ لأنه دين ثابت في الذمة، ولا يتعين بالتعين، ولا فرق بين أن يكون المقبوض من جنسه أو من خلاف جنسه؛ إذ الكل معاوضة، وفي "الغاية": التصرف في الأثمان وسائر الديون من المهر والأجرة وضمان المتلفات ونحوها سوى الصرف والسلم جائز قبل القبض؛ لأن الملك مطلق، وكان القياس أيضاً ذلك في بيع المنقول، إلا أنه ترك بالحديث. رمز الحقائق: ٥٥/٢] (عناية) يسم والزيادة فيه أي وصح للمشتري الزيادة في الثمن، ولو من غير جنسه في المجلس أو بعده، أو من وارث المشتري بشرط قبول البائع في المجلس وبقاء المبيع، وكونه محلا للمقابلة في حق المشتري، وصح للبائع الحط من الثمن، ولو بعد هلاك المبيع وقبض الثمن، فالزيادة والحط يلحقان بأصل العقد ولو بعد تمام العقد، وعند الشافعي وزفر: إلحاقهما بعد لزوم البيع لا يصح، بل يصح على اعتبار أنه يكون صلة مبتدأة فلا إلا بالتسليم؛ لأن المبيع دخل في ملك المشتري، والثمن في ملك البائع، فمن زاد شيئاً، فهو مبدل العوض عن ملك نفسه، وهذا لا يجوز، =
Not the measured by length: i.e., it is not prohibited to dispose of the item sold by length after possession before measuring, even if it was purchased with the condition of measurement; because length measurement is a description, not a quantity, so all of it belongs to the buyer without increase in price or decrease if he finds it more or less. This is if he did not name a price for each cubit. But if he named a price, then it is not permissible for him to dispose of it until he measures, and in case of deficiency, he has the option. (Ayni, Fath) And disposal [i.e., the seller's disposal of the price of the sold item (Ayni)] before its possession is valid, whether it is something unidentifiable like currency or identifiable like measured or weighed items. So if one sells camels for dirhams or a load of wheat, it is permissible to take something else in exchange. This is based on the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'We used to sell camels in al-Baqi' and we would take dinars instead of dirhams, and dirhams instead of dinars, and the Prophet allowed it.' And because the prohibition came for the sold item due to the possibility of uncertainty of rescission, and that is not conceivable in the price because it is a fixed debt in the liability and does not become specific by specification. There is no difference whether what is received is of the same type or a different type, as all are exchanges. In al-Ghayah: Disposal of prices and all debts of dower, rent, compensation for damaged property, and the like excluding [sales of] currency and salam is permissible before possession because ownership is absolute. By analogy, this would also apply to the sale of movable property, but it was abandoned due to the hadith. (Rumuz al-Haqaiq 55/2) (Inayah) And the increase in it: i.e., it is permissible for the buyer to increase the price, even if from a different type, in the session or after it, or from the buyer's heir, on condition that the seller accepts in the session and the sold item remains, and that it is a valid subject for exchange regarding the buyer. And it is permissible for the seller to reduce the price even after the destruction of the sold item and after receiving the price. So the increase and reduction are attached to the original contract even after the contract is complete. According to al-Shafi'i and Zufar, attaching them after the contract is binding is not valid; rather, it is valid only if considered a new gift, so it is not valid without delivery, because the sold item has entered the buyer's ownership and the price into the seller's ownership. So if someone adds something, it becomes an exchange from one's own property, and this is not permissible.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct but sequential topics: (1) Items sold by length (e.g., cloth by the yard) do not require remeasuring after possession; the buyer owns it completely. However, if a price per unit was specified, the buyer must measure before disposal, and a deficiency gives him an option. (2) The seller may dispose of the price (thaman) before receiving it, unlike the sold item. The evidence is the hadith of Ibn Umar where they exchanged currency received from sales before taking possession. The rationale is that the price is a debt in the buyer's liability, not a specific item, so there is no uncertainty of rescission. (3) The buyer may voluntarily increase the price after the contract, and the seller may reduce it; these modifications are effective as part of the original contract, even after payment or destruction of the goods. The Shafi'i school (and Zufar) hold that after the sale is binding, such modifications are new independent gifts requiring delivery. The text supports the Hanafi view that increase and decrease are valid without new delivery.

Key Terms
المذروع (al-madhru'): An item sold by length measurement (e.g., cloth measured in cubits).
الذرع (al-dhara'): Measurement by cubit or other length unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always
B) Never
C) Only if a price per unit was named
D) Only if the buyer intends to resell

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats length as a description, so possession transfers full ownership unless a per-unit price was named, in which case measurement is required before disposal.

Disposal of Price Before Possession and Post-Contract Modifications
Ruling on disposal of price before possession and post-contract modifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits the seller to dispose of the price before possession, and evaluate the validity of post-contract increase or decrease in price.

Core Idea
The price is a debt, not a specific item, so the seller may dispose of it before possession; post-contract modifications attach to the original contract.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses two interconnected issues: the permissibility of the seller using the price before receiving it, and the validity of voluntary price increases or decreases after the contract. The Hanafi position is based on the hadith of Ibn Umar and the nature of the price as a fixed debt. The Shafi'i and Zufar dissent triggers a useful comparative analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling
The seller may dispose of the price (thaman) before taking possession of it. This applies to all debts (currency, measured/weighed items) except in certain sales (sarf, salam).
The price is a debt in the buyer's liability, not a specific item, so there is no risk of rescission (gharar).
2
Identify the proof
The hadith of Ibn Umar: they sold camels and took dinars instead of dirhams, and the Prophet allowed it. Also rational: the prohibition is for the sold item due to potential rescission; the price is a fixed debt.
The hadith is cited from Rumuz al-Haqaiq 55/2.
3
Identify the second ruling
The buyer may increase the price or the seller may decrease it after the contract, even after payment or destruction of goods. These modifications attach to the original contract and do not require a new transaction.
Conditions: buyer's increase requires seller's acceptance in the session, the sold item still exists, and it is a valid subject of exchange for the buyer.
4
Analyze the dispute
Shafi'i and Zufar argue that after the contract is binding, the sold item belongs to the buyer and the price to the seller, so any increase is a new gift requiring delivery. Hanafi responds that the original contract is the basis; modifications are attachments, not new contracts.
This difference leads to different practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(عيني، فتح) وصح التصرف [ أي تصرف البائع في ثمن المبيع. (عيني)] قبل قبضه سواء كان مما لا يتعين كالنقود أو مما يتعين كالمكيل والموزون، حتى لو باع إبلاً بدراهم أو بكر من الحنطة جاز أن يأخذ بدله شيئاً آخر؛ لحديث ابن عمر ما: "كنا نبيع الإبل بالبقيع فنأخذ مكان الدراهم الدنانير، ومكان الدنانير الدراهم، وكان يجوزه رسول الله "، ولأن النهي ورد في المبيع؛ لاحتمال غرر الانفساخ ولا يتصور ذلك في الثمن؛ لأنه دين ثابت في الذمة، ولا يتعين بالتعين، ولا فرق بين أن يكون المقبوض من جنسه أو من خلاف جنسه؛ إذ الكل معاوضة، وفي "الغاية": التصرف في الأثمان وسائر الديون من المهر والأجرة وضمان المتلفات ونحوها سوى الصرف والسلم جائز قبل القبض؛ لأن الملك مطلق، وكان القياس أيضاً ذلك في بيع المنقول، إلا أنه ترك بالحديث. رمز الحقائق: ٥٥/٢] (عناية) يسم والزيادة فيه أي وصح للمشتري الزيادة في الثمن، ولو من غير جنسه في المجلس أو بعده، أو من وارث المشتري بشرط قبول البائع في المجلس وبقاء المبيع، وكونه محلا للمقابلة في حق المشتري، وصح للبائع الحط من الثمن، ولو بعد هلاك المبيع وقبض الثمن، فالزيادة والحط يلحقان بأصل العقد ولو بعد تمام العقد، وعند الشافعي وزفر: إلحاقهما بعد لزوم البيع لا يصح، بل يصح على اعتبار أنه يكون صلة مبتدأة فلا إلا بالتسليم؛ لأن المبيع دخل في ملك المشتري، والثمن في ملك البائع، فمن زاد شيئاً، فهو مبدل العوض عن ملك نفسه، وهذا لا يجوز، =
Not the measured by length: i.e., it is not prohibited to dispose of the item sold by length after possession before measuring, even if it was purchased with the condition of measurement; because length measurement is a description, not a quantity, so all of it belongs to the buyer without increase in price or decrease if he finds it more or less. This is if he did not name a price for each cubit. But if he named a price, then it is not permissible for him to dispose of it until he measures, and in case of deficiency, he has the option. (Ayni, Fath) And disposal [i.e., the seller's disposal of the price of the sold item (Ayni)] before its possession is valid, whether it is something unidentifiable like currency or identifiable like measured or weighed items. So if one sells camels for dirhams or a load of wheat, it is permissible to take something else in exchange. This is based on the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'We used to sell camels in al-Baqi' and we would take dinars instead of dirhams, and dirhams instead of dinars, and the Prophet allowed it.' And because the prohibition came for the sold item due to the possibility of uncertainty of rescission, and that is not conceivable in the price because it is a fixed debt in the liability and does not become specific by specification. There is no difference whether what is received is of the same type or a different type, as all are exchanges. In al-Ghayah: Disposal of prices and all debts of dower, rent, compensation for damaged property, and the like excluding [sales of] currency and salam is permissible before possession because ownership is absolute. By analogy, this would also apply to the sale of movable property, but it was abandoned due to the hadith. (Rumuz al-Haqaiq 55/2) (Inayah) And the increase in it: i.e., it is permissible for the buyer to increase the price, even if from a different type, in the session or after it, or from the buyer's heir, on condition that the seller accepts in the session and the sold item remains, and that it is a valid subject for exchange regarding the buyer. And it is permissible for the seller to reduce the price even after the destruction of the sold item and after receiving the price. So the increase and reduction are attached to the original contract even after the contract is complete. According to al-Shafi'i and Zufar, attaching them after the contract is binding is not valid; rather, it is valid only if considered a new gift, so it is not valid without delivery, because the sold item has entered the buyer's ownership and the price into the seller's ownership. So if someone adds something, it becomes an exchange from one's own property, and this is not permissible.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct but sequential topics: (1) Items sold by length (e.g., cloth by the yard) do not require remeasuring after possession; the buyer owns it completely. However, if a price per unit was specified, the buyer must measure before disposal, and a deficiency gives him an option. (2) The seller may dispose of the price (thaman) before receiving it, unlike the sold item. The evidence is the hadith of Ibn Umar where they exchanged currency received from sales before taking possession. The rationale is that the price is a debt in the buyer's liability, not a specific item, so there is no uncertainty of rescission. (3) The buyer may voluntarily increase the price after the contract, and the seller may reduce it; these modifications are effective as part of the original contract, even after payment or destruction of the goods. The Shafi'i school (and Zufar) hold that after the sale is binding, such modifications are new independent gifts requiring delivery. The text supports the Hanafi view that increase and decrease are valid without new delivery.

Key Terms
الثمن (al-thaman): The price or consideration in a sale; a debt in the buyer's liability until paid.
الزيادة والحط (al-ziyadah wa al-hatt): Increase (by buyer) or decrease (by seller) in the agreed price after the contract is concluded.
لزوم البيع (luzum al-bay'): The binding nature of a sale after which neither party may unilaterally revoke.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, which of the following is NOT permissible without a new transaction?
A) Seller disposing of the price before possession
B) Buyer increasing the price after the contract
C) Seller decreasing the price after the contract
D) Buyer replacing the price with a different item after the contract

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits disposal of the price before possession and allows post-contract price modifications as attachments to the original contract, facilitating commercial flexibility.
