10 min
Disposition of Sold Goods Before Measurement
Ruling on disposing of makil/mawzun/ma'dud before weighing/counting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on disposing of measured/weighed/counted goods before re-measurement and identify the exceptions.

Core Idea
A buyer cannot sell or consume weighed/measured/counted goods until re-measurement—except in hand-to-hand sales and currency.

In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of a sale depends on certainty of quantity. This passage from Kanz al-Daqā’iq establishes a key rule: the buyer must re-measure or re-weigh certain types of goods before disposing of them, lest the transaction involve gharar or ribā. However, the text outlines important exceptions that every student must know.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories and the general rule
Recognize that the rule applies to makīl (measured by volume), mawzūn (weighed), and ma‘dūd (counted) items. The buyer cannot sell, eat, or otherwise dispose of them until re-measuring/weighing/counting.
This is the default ruling for regular sales.
2
Note the exceptions
Three exceptions: (1) bay‘ al-ta‘ātī (hand-to-hand sale) – the initial measurement suffices; (2) dirhams and dīnārs (currency) – no re-weighing needed; (3) when the sold item itself is the price (thaman) – disposal before measurement is allowed.
The muftā bihi is that bay‘ al-ta‘ātī does not require re-measurement.
3
Trace the intra-madhhab dispute on ma‘dūd
Abū Ḥanīfah considers counted items like measured/weighed (must re-count). The two companions (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad) consider them like length-measured items (no re-counting needed). The relied-upon view is Abū Ḥanīfah’s.
This dispute is a legitimate ikhtilāf within the madhhab.
4
Understand the ruling for madhrū‘
Length-measured items (e.g., cloth) generally can be disposed before re-measurement. However, if the contract specifies a price per unit length, re-measurement becomes required and deficiency gives the buyer an option (khiyār).
The default is that measuring length is a description, not a quantity.
5
Apply the rule to a practical scenario
Consider a buyer who purchases 5 liters of milk (makīl) in a regular sale. He must re-measure before drinking or selling any. If he buys via bay‘ al-ta‘ātī, he may drink immediately.
Always check which category and exception apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يصح بيعه حتى يكيله، ومثله: الموزون والمعدود، لا المذرُوع، وصح التصرف في الثمن قبل قبضه والزيادة فيه. الثمن الموزون إلخ: لا يجوز للمشتري أن يبيع الموزون والمعدود، أو يأكل منهما حتى يعيد الوزن والعدد، وهو مقيد بغير بيع التعاطي، أما إذا كان البيع بالتعاطي، فلا يحتاج إلى إعادة الوزن ثانياً؛ لأنه صار بيعاً بالقبض بعد الوزن، وعليه الفتوى، ومقيد أيضاً بغير الدراهم والدنانير، فيجوز التصرف فيهما بعد القبض قبل الوزن. وفي "المحيط": لو كان المكيل والموزون ثمناً يجوز التصرف فيه قبل الكيل والوزن ولو كاله البائع بحضرة المشتري بعد البيع قبل القبض، قيل: لا يكتفي به؛ لظاهر الحديث، فإنه اشترط فيه صاعين والصحيح أنه يكتفي به؛ لأن المبيع صار معلوماً بكيل واحد، وتحقق معنى التسليم، والحديث محمول على ما إذا اجتمعت الصفقتان على ما نبينه في باب السلم، وجعل المصنف المعدود كالمكيل والموزون، وهو مروي عن أبي حنيفة، وعنه: أنه كالمذروع، وهو قول الصاحبين. لا المذروع: أي لا يحرم التصرف في المبيع المذروع بعد القبض قبل الذرع وإن اشتراه بشرط الذرع؛ لأن الذرع وصف له، وليس بقدر، فيكون كله للمشتري بلا زيادة ثمن ولا نقصان إن وجده زائداً أو ناقصاً، هذا إذا لم لكل ذراع ثمنا، وإن سمى فلا يحل له التصرف فيه حتى يذرع، وفي النقصان يثبت له الخيار.
What is valid to sell until he measures it. And like it: weighed and counted items, not the measured-by-length (madhrū‘). And disposal of the price before its receipt and increase in it is valid. The weighed price, etc.: It is not permissible for the buyer to sell weighed or counted items, or to eat from them, until he repeats the weighing and counting. This is restricted to other than bay‘ al-ta‘ātī (hand-to-hand sale). As for if the sale was by hand-to-hand, he does not need to repeat the weighing a second time because it became a sale by possession after weighing, and upon this is the fatwā. It is also restricted to other than dirhams and dinars, so disposal of them after possession before weighing is permissible. In al-Muḥīṭ: If the measured or weighed item was a price, it is permissible to dispose of it before measurement or weighing. Even if the seller measured it in the presence of the buyer after the sale but before possession, it is said: it is not sufficient due to the apparent meaning of the hadith, for it stipulated two ṣā‘s. The correct view is that it is sufficient because the sold item becomes known by one measurement and the meaning of delivery is realized. The hadith is interpreted as when two transactions combined as we will explain in the chapter on salam. The author considered counted items like measured and weighed items, which is narrated from Abū Ḥanīfah. From him also: it is like measured-by-length, and that is the view of the two companions (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad). Not the measured-by-length: i.e., it is not prohibited to dispose of the measured-by-length sold item after possession before measuring by length, even if he bought it with the condition of measuring by length, because measuring by length is a description of it, not a quantity. So it all belongs to the buyer without increase or decrease in price if he finds it extra or deficient. This is if there is not for each cubit a price, and if he specified a price for each cubit, then it is not permissible for him to dispose of it until he measures by length, and in case of deficiency he has the option.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqā’iq deals with a key principle: the buyer cannot dispose of certain types of goods (measured, weighed, counted) by sale or consumption until they have been re-measured/weighed/counted after possession. This is because the exact quantity is not yet known to the buyer with certainty, and disposing before ascertainment may lead to ribā or gharar. However, this rule has exceptions: (1) bay‘ al-ta‘ātī (hand-to-hand sale) where the exchange is immediate, so the initial measurement suffices—this is the relied-upon position (muftā bihi). (2) Dirhams and dīnārs (currency) are excluded; they can be disposed of after possession even without re-weighing because they are intended as mediums of exchange. (3) If the sold item itself is used as the price (thaman) in a transaction, disposal before measurement is allowed because it is being treated as a debt. The author also discusses an intra-madhhab dispute: Abū Ḥanīfah initially counted 'counted items' (ma‘dūd) together with measured and weighed, but he also had a narration equating them with measured-by-length (madhrū‘), which is the position of the two companions (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad). For items measured by length (like cloth), disposal is normally allowed before measuring, unless the contract specifies a price per unit length, in which case re-measurement is required and deficiency gives the buyer an option (khiyār).

Key Terms
المكيل (al-makīl): Items sold by volume (e.g., grains, liquids).
الموزون (al-mawzūn): Items sold by weight (e.g., gold, silver, meat).
المعدود (al-ma‘dūd): Items sold by count (e.g., eggs, fruits).
المذروع (al-madhrū‘): Items sold by length measurement (e.g., cloth, rope).
بيع التعاطي (bay‘ al-ta‘ātī): A hand-to-hand sale where exchange is immediate, often without verbal statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, when is it permissible for the buyer to dispose of a weighed item (mawzūn) after purchase without re-weighing?
A) In all cases, possession alone suffices.
B) If the sale was by hand-to-hand exchange (bay‘ al-ta‘ātī).
C) Only if the item is also madhrū‘.
D) Never; re-weighing is always required.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales law, the buyer of measured, weighed, or counted goods must re-determine the quantity before disposal, unless the sale was hand-to-hand or the goods are currency, and length-measured items are generally exempt except when sold per unit length.

Rulings on Reduction, Increase, and Deferment in Sales
Explains validity and effects of post-contract modifications and debt deferment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on reduction (hatt) and increase (ziyada) in sales, explain the exception for an agent's reduction, and identify when deferment (ta'jil) of a debt is valid and binding.

Core Idea
Reduction and increase after a sale attach to the original contract; only the agent's reduction is excluded.

After a sale contract is concluded, parties may wish to modify the terms—reducing the price or increasing the goods. In Hanafi law, such modifications are valid and attach to the original contract, based on the principle that the authority to cancel the contract includes the authority to change its description. There are important nuances, especially when an agent acts for the seller. Additionally, deferring a debt from immediate to future payment is generally valid, except for loans (qard). This lesson unpacks these rules and their underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
Recognize the three legal acts discussed: reduction of price (hatt), increase of sold item (ziyada), and deferment of debt (ta'jil). For each, note the basic ruling: valid and effective (sahih).
The text also covers reduction of the sold item itself, which has a special condition.
2
Understand the talil (reasoning)
The proof given is: the parties have the right to cancel the contract entirely, so changing its description (e.g., from loss to profit) is even more permissible (awla). This qiyas-like argument establishes the validity of modifications.
This reasoning is specific to the Hanafi school.
3
Apply the exception for agents
Note that if an agent (wakil) reduces the price, the reduction does not attach to the contract. The agent becomes liable to the principal (seller) for the amount reduced, and the pre-emptor (shafi') takes the property at the full price.
This is a key boundary condition.
4
Analyze the effects
Understand the practical consequences: the buyer must pay the increase to demand delivery; the seller may withhold delivery until full payment (including increase); if a defect in title appears, the buyer recovers the increase from the seller.
These effects show that the modification is integrated into the contract.
5
Distinguish the deferment rules
Deferment (ta'jil) of an immediate debt is valid with the debtor's acceptance, except for a loan (qard). For loans, deferment is not binding because a loan is a gratuitous contract (ariyah). Note the cross-madhhab views: Shafi'i rejects deferment validity; Maliki accepts it even for loans.
The bequest case shows an exception to the loan rule due to leniency in bequests.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحط منه القرض.

والزيادة في المبيع، ويتعلق الاستحقاق بكله، وصح تأجيل كلّ دين غير
يصح؛
لأنه
ولنا: أنهما يغيران بهما صفة العقد من الخسارة إلى الربح أو العدل، ولهما دفع العقد، فلأن يكون لهما تغيير وصفه أولى. والحط منه: أي وصح للبائع الحط من الثمن للمشتري بعد تعيينه فيه. والزيادة: أي وصح للبائع الزيادة في المبيع بعد علم المشتري بمقداره. وصح للبائع الزيادة في المبيع، ولا يشترط قيام المبيع، بخلاف الزيادة في الثمن، وأما الحط من المبيع، ففي "المحيط": إن كان ديناً يصح، وإن كان عيناً لا إسقاط، وإسقاط العين لا يصح، وتلحق الزيادة بأصل العقد خلافاً للشافعي، وزفر، واعلم أن التحاق الحط بأصل العقد مقيد بما إذا لم يكن من الوكيل، حتى لو حط الوكيل ببيع الدار عن المشتري مائة صح، وضمن للموكل، ويأخذها الشفيع بجميع الثمن؛ لأن حط الوكيل لا يلتحق بأصل العقد. ويتعلق إلخ: أي بكل ما وقع عليه في العقد من حط الثمن الأول والزيادة عليه، حتى لا يكون للمشتري أن يطالب بالمبيع حتى يدفع الزيادة، وللبائع أن يحبسه حتى يستوفي الثمن، والزيادة، ويملك المشتري المطالبة بتسليم كله وبتسليم ما بقي من الحط، وإذا ظهر للمبيع مستحق يرجع المشتري على البائع بالزيادة، وليس للبائع أن يمتنع من تسليم الزيادة. الاستحقاق: أي استحقاق البائع والمشتري في الثمن والمبيع. بكله : أي بكل ما وقع عليه العقد من الثمن والمبيع والزيادة والحط. تأجيل: أي دين حال سواء كان ثمنا أو غيره، حتى لو باعه شيئاً بثمن حال ثم أجل أجلا معلوما صار مؤجلا ؛ لأن المطالبة حقه فله أن يؤخره بشرط قبول المديون، حتى لو رده بقي الشافعي له في قول: لا يصح تأجيل الدين. غير القرض فإن تأجيله لا يلزم حتى لو أجله عند الإقراض مدة معلومة أو بعده لا يثبت الأجل وله أ في الحال؛ لأن القرض إعارة وهي تبرع والتأجيل في الإعارة ليس بلازم؛ لأنها تبرع، وقال مالك له: يجوز التأجيل أي يلزم في القرض أيضاً كسائر الديون ولو أوصى بأن يقرض من ماله ألف درهم فلاناً إلى سنة، وهو يخرج من ثلث ماله، يلزم الورثة أن يقرضوه ولا يطالبوه قبل المدة؛ لأنه وصية بالتبرع، ويتسامح فيها ما لا يتسامح في غيرها نظراً للموصي، ألا ترى أنها تجوز بالخدمة والسكنى وتلزم حالا، وعند
And reduction from it is the loan. The sold item. It is not valid to sell it. And the increase in the sold item, and entitlement attaches to all of it, and it is valid to defer every debt except the loan. It is not valid; because. And for us: that they change by them the description of the contract from loss to profit or justice, and they have the right to cancel the contract, so it is more appropriate that they have the right to change its description. And reduction from it: meaning it is valid for the seller to reduce the price for the buyer after specifying it. And the increase: meaning it is valid for the seller to increase the sold item after the buyer knows its amount. And it is valid for the seller to increase the sold item, and the existence of the sold item is not a condition, unlike the increase in the price. As for reduction from the sold item, in al-Muhit: if it is a debt, it is valid; if it is a specific good, it cannot be dropped, and dropping a specific good is not valid. And the increase attaches to the original contract, contrary to al-Shafi'i and Zufar. And know that the attachment of reduction to the original contract is conditional on it not being from the agent; such that if the agent reduces the price in a sale of a house for the buyer by one hundred, it is valid, and he is liable to the principal, and the pre-emptor takes it with the full price; because the reduction by the agent does not attach to the original contract. 'And it attaches' etc.: meaning to everything that was agreed upon in the contract of reduction of the first price and increase upon it, such that the buyer cannot demand the sold item until he pays the increase, and the seller has the right to withhold it until he receives the price and the increase, and the buyer has the right to demand delivery of all of it and delivery of what remains after the reduction, and if the sold item turns out to be owned by someone else, the buyer recovers the increase from the seller, and the seller is not allowed to refrain from delivering the increase. Entitlement: meaning the entitlement of the seller and buyer in the price and the sold item. 'In all of it': meaning everything that the contract covered of the price, sold item, increase, and reduction. Deferment: meaning an immediate debt, whether it is a price or something else; such that if he sold him something for an immediate price then deferred it for a known period, it becomes deferred; because the right of demand is his, so he may postpone it on condition of the debtor's acceptance; such that if he refuses, it remains immediate. Al-Shafi'i has a saying: deferment of a debt is not valid. Except the loan: its deferment is not binding; even if he defers it at the time of lending for a known period or afterwards, the deferment is not established, and he has the right to demand it immediately; because lending is a loan (ariyah) and it is a gratuitous contract, and deferment in a gratuitous contract is not binding because it is gratuitous. Malik said: deferment is permissible, i.e., binding in loans as well like other debts. And if he bequeathed that from his wealth one thousand dirhams be lent to so-and-so for one year, and it comes out of one third of his wealth, the heirs are obliged to lend it to him and not demand it before the term; because it is a bequest of a gratuity, and leniency is shown in it that is not shown in other things out of consideration for the testator; do you not see that it is valid for service and residence and binds immediately? And upon.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses two key issues in sales contracts: reduction (hatt) and increase (ziyada) after the contract, and deferment (ta'jil) of debts. The author first establishes that both reduction of the price by the seller and increase of the sold item by the seller are valid and attach to the original contract, meaning the contract remains the same but with modified terms. This is based on the reasoning (talil) that the parties have the right to change the description of the contract (from loss to profit or justice), just as they have the right to cancel it entirely. There is a dispute with al-Shafi'i and Zufar, who hold that increase does not attach to the original contract. The Hanafi position is that it does, except in the case of an agent (wakil): if an agent reduces the price, it does not attach to the contract, so the agent is liable to the principal and the pre-emptor takes the property at the full price. For reduction of the sold item itself (not the price), it is only valid if it is a debt (dayn), not a specific good ('ayn), because dropping a specific good is not possible. The passage then discusses the effects: the buyer cannot demand delivery until paying the increase; the seller may withhold until full payment; the buyer may demand delivery of the entire item including any increase; if a defect in title appears, the buyer recovers the increase from the seller. The second part covers deferment of debts: any immediate debt can be deferred by agreement, except a loan (qard). For a loan, deferment is not binding because a loan is a gratuitous contract (ariyah) and gratuitous contracts do not require commitment of deferment. Al-Shafi'i holds that deferment of any debt is invalid (i.e., does not change its immediate nature), while Malik holds that deferment is binding even for loans. The passage ends with a special case of a bequest (wasiyyah) to lend money for a term: this is binding on the heirs because it is a bequest of a gratuity, and leniency is shown.

Key Terms
الحط (al-hatt): Reduction of the price by the seller after the contract.
الزيادة (al-ziyada): Increase in the sold item by the seller after the contract.
التأجيل (al-ta'jil): Deferment of an immediate debt to a future date.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a seller reduces the price after selling a house, does the reduction attach to the original contract?
A) Yes, always.
B) Yes, unless the reduction was done by an agent.
C) No, it requires a new contract.
D) No, reduction is not allowed after contract.

Key Takeaway
Reduction and increase after sale are valid and attach to the contract, except when done by an agent; deferment binds all debts except loans.

12 min
The Cause of Riba: Hanafi View on Capacity and Genus
Defines riba and discusses its cause across madhhabs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi cause of riba, distinguish it from the Shafi'i and Maliki positions, and apply it to classify a transaction as ribawi or not.

Core Idea
The Hanafi cause of riba is capacity and genus—not taste or storability.

The prohibition of riba (usury) is universally accepted, but the schools differ on what exactly triggers it. The Hanafi school, drawing on explicit prophetic commands, identifies the cause as a compound of capacity (measure/weight) and genus (same type of commodity). This lesson examines the Hanafi argument and its response to the Shafi'i and Maliki alternatives.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi cause of riba
Identify the complete cause as qadr (capacity: measure for measurable, weight for weighable) and jins (genus: both countervalues of the same type). Also note the incomplete cause when only one is present.
The incomplete cause prohibits figurative surplus (e.g., credit).
2
Identify the opponent's view and their evidence
State the Shafi'i position (cause is taste in food and currency in money) and the Maliki position (sustenance/storability plus genus in food). Note their primary hadith evidence.
Shafi'i relies on 'Food for food, like for like.'
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof from hadith
Examine three hadiths: 'Wheat for wheat, like for like...', 'Do not sell a dirham for two dirhams', and 'Whatever is weighed, like for like if one type.' Explain how each links the ruling to capacity and genus.
The dirham hadith extends the prohibition beyond food.
4
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal
Explain why the Hanafi school rejects taste/storability as the sole cause: the dirham example (non-food, no taste) is included, so the cause must be broader. Capacity and genus cover both food and non-food items.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical difference: Under Hanafi, all measurable/weighable items of the same genus are subject to riba rules (e.g., iron, dates); under Shafi'i, only food items with taste and monetary items; under Maliki, only staple foods plus monetary items.
This affects muamalat in trade.

باب الربا أي في بيان أحكامه فضلُ مال بلا عوض في معاوضة مال بمال، وعلّته القدرُ والجنس. أي الربا شرعاً في مقابلة باب الربا: تناسب البابين من حيث أن فيهما زيادة لكن في المرابحة زيادة هي حلال، وفي الربا Chapter on Riba: i.e., explaining its rulings. Surplus of property without compensation in exchange of property for property. And its cause is capacity and genus. i.e., riba legally in exchange. Chapter on riba: similarity of the two chapters in that both have increase, but in murabahah the increase is halal, and in riba the increase is haram, and avoiding doubtful matters is obligatory in every chapter. And it [riba] linguistically is absolute increase, from 'raba al-mal' when it increases. And its prohibition is by the three proofs: Book, Sunnah, and Consensus, and therefore the one who considers it permissible becomes a disbeliever. 'Surplus': i.e., increase of property even if virtual. 'In exchange of property': i.e., mostly, and it is conditional for one of the two contractors. 'And its cause': i.e., the cause of obligation of equality which if absent necessitates riba, or the cause of the property being riba and the cause of prohibition of surplus. The cause is of two types: complete cause, which is capacity and genus; and incomplete cause, which is capacity without genus or genus without capacity. And surplus is also of two types: real surplus like selling one dirham for two dirhams, and figurative surplus like selling one dirham for one dirham on credit. So the complete cause prohibits real surplus, and the incomplete cause prohibits figurative surplus. It is apparent that the pronoun 'its cause' refers to measure and weighed items of the same genus similarly – riba, and it is invalid because it is valid with the existence of the cause. We say: the meaning of our statement 'the cause of riba is capacity and genus' is the cause of obligation of equality which necessitates riba when it is absent. And his statement: 'capacity' is an expression for equality in form, so similitude is established by it in both. 'Capacity etc.': i.e., the cause of prohibition of surplus according to us is composed of two parts: capacity, meaning measure in measurable items and weight in weighable items, and genus which is that the two countervalues are of one genus. The basis for it is the famous hadith which is his statement: 'Wheat for wheat, like for like, hand to hand, and the excess is riba.' i.e., sell like for like, or sell wheat for wheat like for like, and the report has the meaning of a command. Since the command indicates obligation, and sale is permissible, the obligation is directed to observing similitude. Similitude between two things is considered both in form and meaning: capacity equalizes form, and genuses equalize meaning, so the surplus which is riba becomes apparent. So the cause according to us has two parts. And Ahmad said the same, and from him regarding non-numismatic things it is being edible and [being of the same] genus. According to al-Shafi'i: the cause is taste in food items and currency [value] in monetary items. Ahmad [ibn Hanbal] said in one narration: due to the hadith, and he said: I heard the Prophet say: 'Food for food, like for like, and our food at that time was barley.' Narrated by Muslim. And Ahmad made similitude a condition and ascribed the cause to the description of taste, so it was the cause. And for us: his statement: 'Do not sell a dirham for two dirhams, nor a sa' for two sa'' is general regarding what he made lawful, so it includes food and non-food. And Malik said: the cause is sustenance and storability with genus in food items; because upon that [basis] every sustained and stored item was specifically mentioned; and because the risk and danger in it are more complete, so it was more appropriate and more entitled to consideration. And he said regarding monetary items like al-Shafi'i. And for us: what is narrated from 'Ubada and Anas that the Prophet said: 'Whatever is weighed, [sell] like for like if it is one type, and whatever is measured, similarly; and if the types differ, then there is no harm.' Narrated by al-Daraqutni. He based the ruling on capacity and genus.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq opens the chapter on riba (usury/interest) by defining it and establishing its cause ('illa). It begins by stating that riba legally is 'surplus of property without compensation in an exchange of property for property.' The cause of riba is capacity (qadr: measure for measureable goods, weight for weighable goods) and genus (jins: both countervalues being of the same type). The author explains that the cause can be complete (both qadr and jins) which prohibits real surplus (e.g., selling one dirham for two), or incomplete (only qadr or only jins) which prohibits figurative surplus (e.g., selling one dirham for one dirham on credit). The passage delves into an inter-madhhab dispute over the correct cause of riba. The Hanafi position, supported by Imam Ahmad in one narration, is that the cause is qadr and jins. This is derived from the famous hadith: 'Wheat for wheat, like for like, hand to hand, and the excess is riba,' and also from the general command 'Do not sell a dirham for two dirhams.' The Hanafi argument is that these texts base the ruling on capacity and genus, not on taste or food value. Al-Shafi'i holds that the cause is taste (tu'm) in food items and currency in monetary items, citing the hadith 'Food for food, like for like.' The Hanafi response is that the prohibition of selling dirham for two dirhams is general and includes both food and non-food, so the cause must be broader. Malik holds that the cause is sustenance (iqtit) and storability (iddikhar) with genus in food items, and for monetary items he agrees with al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi proof includes the hadith from 'Ubada and Anas where the Prophet explicitly ties the ruling to weight and measure, confirming the two-part cause. The passage also notes that riba is prohibited by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma', and that considering it halal leads to disbelief.

Key Terms
الربا (al-riba): Surplus of property without compensation in an exchange of property for property.
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause that necessitates the ruling of prohibition of riba.
القدر (al-qadr): Capacity – measured for measurable items, weight for weighable items.
الجنس (al-jins): Genus – the two countervalues being of the same type.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the complete cause ('illa) of riba?
A) Taste (tu'm) alone.
B) Sustenance and storability (iqtit and iddikhar).
C) Capacity (qadr) and genus (jins).
D) Currency value (thamaniyya) alone.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi cause of riba is capacity and genus, making it broader than other schools.

The Fourfold Cause of Riba and the Dispute on Jins Alone
Defines riba types and fourfold cause-effect relation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when jins alone prohibits riba al-nasa' and distinguish it from the Shafi'i view by applying the fourfold cause framework.

Core Idea
Jins alone prohibits deferment (nasa') but not excess (fadl) — a shubha of riba suffices.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq defines two types of riba and the conditions that trigger each. The Hanafi school introduces a sophisticated fourfold categorization of causes and effects to justify why a single condition (jins or qadr) can prohibit credit sales even without excess. We will unpack that framework and the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Identify the ruling: when both jins and qadr are present, both fadl and nasa' are haram; when only one is present, only nasa' is haram. The proof is a rational argument based on the concept of shubhat al-illa.
2
State the opponent's position
Al-Shafi'i holds that jins alone does not prohibit nasa'; a complete cause (both jins and qadr) is required for any prohibition.
3
Follow the Hanafi response using the fourfold division
The Hanafi response distinguishes between haqiqat al-illa (both jins and qadr) which prohibits haqiqat al-riba (fadl), and shubhat al-illa (one of them) which prohibits shubhat al-riba (nasa').
This shows why a single condition can prohibit nasa' but not fadl.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi prohibits selling wheat for wheat on credit even if equal; Shafi'i permits it.
5
Note the tarjih (mufta bihi position)
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon view; the commentary by Ayni and Fath al-Qadir confirms it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الربا

كتاب البيوع فحرُمَ الفضلُ والنَّساء بهما، والنساء فقط بأحدهما، وحلّا بعدمهما، وصح بيعُ الجنس والقدر أي وحرم النساء دون الفضل التفاضل والنساء جميعا

المكيل كالبر والشعير والثمر والملح والموزون كالنقدين، وما ينسب إلى الرطل من المعيار بيع الدراهم والدنانير أي وصح أيضاً بيع ما إلخ

وهو نص على أنهما علة الحكم؛ لأن ترتب الحكم على الاسم المشتق ينبئ عن علية مأخذ الاشتقاق لذلك الحكم، فيكون تقديره : المكيل والموزون مثلاً بمثل بسبب الكيل أو الوزن مع الجنس فيكون حجة عليهما، وعلم هذا أن ما لا يكال ولا يوزن لا يكون من أموال الربوية ولهذا قالوا لا يجري الربا فيما لا يدخل تحت كالحفنة من الحنطة والشعير، وكالذرة من الذهب والفضة؛ لعدم الدخول تحت المعيار، ويبتني على الأصل المذكور فروع كثيرة، منها: إذا باع حفنة من الطعام بحفنتين منه يجوز عندنا، وعند الثلاثة: لا، إلا في رواية عن أحمد ومالك، ومنها: لو باع كيلاً من زبيب بكيلين منه لا يجوز إجماعاً؛ لوجود المعيار، ومنها: لو باع حفنة من ملح بحفنتين منه، يجوز إجماعاً. (عيني، فتح) فحرم إلخ: أي متى وجد القدر والجنس، حرم الفضل والنساء مطلقاً، سواء كان في المطعوم أو غيره، فلا يجوز الحنطة بالحنطة متفاضلاً أو بنساء أي البيع إلى أجل. والنساء فقط أي حرم البيع إلى أجل دون الفضل بوجود القدر أو الجنس، فيجوز بيع البر بالشعير متفاضلاً يداً بيد لا نسيئة، وكذا بيع الهروي بالهروي يجوز يداً بيد لا نسيئة وقال الشافعي: الجنس بانفراده لا يحرم النساء، لا يقال: أحدهما جزء العلة، وبه لا يثبت الحكم، فكيف يثبت بأحدهما حرمة النساء؛ لأنا نقول: إن أحد جزئي العلة شبهة العلة وشبهة العلة لا تحرم إلا لشبهة الربا، وهو النساء، وبحقيقة العلة وهي جزئا العلة تحرم حقيقة الربا، وهي التفاضل والحاصل: أن ههنا أشياء أربعة أحدها حقيقة العلة، والثاني : شبهة العلة والثالث حقيقة الربا والرابع شبهة الربا، فحقيقة الربا يثبت بحقيقة العلة، و شبهة الربا بشبهة العلة، ولا ينعكس. (عيني، فتح)
Chapter of Riba. Book of Sales. So excess and deferment are prohibited together, and deferment alone is prohibited with one of them, and both are permissible in their absence. And the sale of the genus and measure is valid, meaning deferment is prohibited without excess, and excess and deferment are both [prohibited] together. The measured like wheat, barley, dates, salt, and the weighed like the two metals (gold and silver), and what is attributed to the ratl from the standard. The sale of dirhams and dinars... And it is a text that they are the cause of the ruling; because the attachment of the ruling to the derived name indicates the causality of the derivation source for that ruling. So its estimation is: the measured and weighed like for like due to measure or weight with the genus, so it is evidence against them. And from this it is known that what is not measured or weighed is not from the ribawi properties. For this they said: riba does not apply to what does not fall under the standard, like a handful of wheat or barley, and like a grain of gold or silver, due to not falling under the standard. And upon this mentioned principle many branches are built: including: if one sells a handful of food for two handfuls of the same, it is permissible with us (Hanafis), and with the three (other imams) it is not, except in a narration from Ahmad and Malik. And including: if one sells a measured quantity of raisins for two measured quantities of the same, it is not permissible by consensus, due to the existence of the standard. And including: if one sells a handful of salt for two handfuls of the same, it is permissible by consensus. (Ayni, Fath) 'So forbade, etc.' meaning: whenever measure (qadr) and genus (jins) are found, excess and deferment are absolutely forbidden, whether in food or other. So wheat for wheat with excess or on credit is not permissible. 'Deferment only' means the sale on credit is forbidden without excess by the existence of measure or genus. So barley for wheat with excess hand-to-hand is permissible, not on credit. Similarly, the sale of [two types of a commodity] hand-to-hand is permissible, not on credit. And al-Shafi'i said: the genus alone does not forbid deferment. It is not said: one of them is part of the cause, and by it the ruling is not established. So how is the prohibition of deferment established by one of them? Because we say: one of the two parts of the cause is a semblance of the cause (shubhat al-illa), and the semblance of the cause only prohibits due to the semblance of riba, which is deferment, while by the reality of the cause (haqiqat al-illa), which is both parts of the cause, the reality of riba is prohibited, which is excess. The result: here are four things: one is the reality of the cause, the second is the semblance of the cause, the third is the reality of riba, and the fourth is the semblance of riba. So the reality of riba is established by the reality of the cause, and the semblance of riba by the semblance of the cause, and it is not reversed. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the conditions for riba. The Hanafi school holds that riba al-fadl (excess) and riba al-nasa' (deferment) are prohibited when both jins (same species) and qadr (standard measure/weight) are present. If only one of these conditions exists, then only riba al-nasa' is prohibited, not riba al-fadl. Al-Shafi'i argues that jins alone does not prohibit deferment. The Hanafi response introduces a fourfold division: the reality of the cause (haqiqat al-illa) is both jins and qadr together, which prohibits the reality of riba (excess). The semblance of the cause (shubhat al-illa) is either jins or qadr alone, which prohibits the semblance of riba (deferment). This analysis shows that jins or qadr individually create a Shubha (doubt) of riba, sufficient to prohibit deferment but not excess.

Key Terms
الربا (al-ribā): An unlawful excess or deferment in exchange of certain goods.
الفضل (al-faḍl): Excess in quantity when exchanging same-type ribawi items.
النساء (al-nasāʾ): Deferment of delivery or payment in exchange.
العلة (al-ʿilla): The effective cause that brings about the legal ruling (here, prohibition of riba).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, which of the following is prohibited?
A) Selling wheat for barley on credit without excess
B) Selling wheat for wheat with excess but immediate delivery
C) Selling barley for barley in equal amount on credit
D) Selling a handful of salt for two handfuls of salt hand-to-hand

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits credit sales (riba al-nasa') when the same species (jins) is involved, even if no excess, because a single part of the cause creates a semblance of riba.

Textually Defined Ribawi Items: A Permanent Classification
Defines ribawi items as measured or weighed and establishes permanence of classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that textually designated measured/weighed items retain their classification forever and apply it to determine the validity of an exchange.

Core Idea
Whatever the Lawgiver has designated as measured or weighed remains so forever, even if people change their practice.

In this passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq, the author establishes a foundational principle of Hanafi riba law: items that the Lawgiver explicitly categorized as measured (makil) or weighed (mawzun) retain that status permanently. This classification cannot be overridden by subsequent changes in customary practice. Understanding this permanence is crucial for correctly identifying which items are subject to riba in exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual designation
The Lawgiver has explicitly stated that certain items are measured (e.g., wheat) or weighed (e.g., gold). Recognize that this is a textual (nass) designation.
These items are known from the hadith.
2
Apply the permanence rule
Once designated, the item's classification as makil or mawzun is fixed forever, even if people stop measuring or weighing it that way.
This is a qa'ida: 'al-mansus 'alayhi kadhalika abadan'.
3
Analyze an exchange scenario
If someone sells a textually measured item by weight (or vice versa), the sale is not valid unless equality is confirmed by the original standard.
Even if the quantities by weight are equal, the original standard must be used.
4
Distinguish textual from customary items
Items without text are subject to custom, but here the focus is on textually designated items.
Custom cannot override text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفضل أي فضل أحد العوضين على الآخر. (كفاية) والنساء: النساء بفتح النون والمد، وهو التأخير. (عيني، مسكين) وصح بيع المكيل [ أي الذي يدخل تحت الكيل. (عيني) ما نص الشارع على أنه مكيل أو موزون، فهو كذلك أبداً، وإن ترك الناس ذلك، حتى لو باع المكيل وزناً أو الموزون كيلاً لا يجوز، وإن تساويا فيما بيعا به، حتى يعلم تساويهما بالأصالة، وما لا نص فيه تعتبر العادة، وعن أبي يوسف أن العرف على خلاف المنصوص عليه معتبر؛ لأن النص عليه في ذلك الوقت إنما كان للعادة، فكانت. المنظور إليه في ذلك الوقت، وقد تبدلت. (فتح) والموزون أي وصح الموزون الذي يدخل تحت الوزن. (عيني) الرطل الرطل - بكسر الراء وفتحها نصف منّ، وهو ما يوزن به، وفي البناية أنه اثنا عشر أوقية أي كل شيء وقع عليه كيل الرطل؛ فإنه موزون مثل الأدهان؛ فإنها لا تستمسك إلا في وعاء وفي وزن كل وعاء، حرج الرطل لذلك تيسيراً، والمراد به وعاء معلوم الوزن، وقال قاضي خان تفسيره أن ما يباع بالأواقي فهو وزني؛ لأن الأواقي قدرت بطريق الوزن فصارت وزنياً، وأما سائر المكاييل ما قدرت وزنه فهو كيلي ولا يكون وزنياً، = هي فاتخذ
Al-fadl: the excess of one consideration over the other. (Kifayah) Al-nasa': with fat-ha on the nun and madd, meaning deferment. (Ayni, Miskeen) And the sale of measured (items) is valid: meaning that which falls under measure. (Ayni) Whatever the Lawgiver has stated as measured or weighed is so forever, even if people abandon that, so that if one sells a measured item by weight or a weighed item by measure, it is not permissible, even if they are equal in what they are sold for, until their equality is known originally. And what there is no text about, custom is considered. And from Abu Yusuf: that custom contrary to the text is considered; because the text at that time was only due to custom, so it was the object of consideration at that time, and it has changed. (Fath) And al-mawzun: meaning the sale of weighed items that fall under weight is valid. (Ayni) Al-ratl: with kasr of the ra' and its fatha, half a mann, and it is what is weighed with. In al-Binaya it is twelve uqiyas, i.e., everything to which the measure of the ratl applies: it is weighed, like oils; because they are only contained in a vessel and in the weight of each vessel the ratl is difficult, so for ease. And what is meant is a vessel of known weight. Qadi Khan said its interpretation: what is sold by the uqiya is weight-based; because the uqiyas were determined by way of weight, so they became weight-based. As for other measures that were not determined by weight, they are volume-based and not weight-based.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the definition of ribawi items. It states that the sale of measured or weighed items is valid. The text establishes a principle: items explicitly designated by the Lawgiver as measured (like wheat) or weighed (like gold) retain that status permanently, even if people change their practice. For example, selling a measured item by weight does not make it permissible unless equality is known by its original standard. For items without explicit textual designation, local custom determines whether they are measured or weighed. Abu Yusuf holds that even if custom contradicts an earlier text, custom is considered because the text originally relied on custom. The passage also clarifies terms: al-ratl is a weight unit, and items sold by uqiya are weight-based. This affects whether riba applies: only items that are measured or weighed by standard are subject to riba.

Key Terms
المكيل (al-makīl): Items measured by volume according to Shariah or custom.
الموزون (al-mawzūn): Items weighed by standard weight units.
العادة (al-ʿāda): Custom of the people in determining measurement/weight standards.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling if someone sells a measured item (like wheat) by weight and the quantities are equal?
A) Valid, because the quantities are equal
B) Invalid, until equality is known by the original standard (volume)
C) Valid only if done by custom
D) Invalid in all cases

Key Takeaway
The Lawgiver's classification of an item as measured or weighed is permanent and cannot be overridden by subsequent changes in custom.

The Role of Custom and Abu Yusuf's View on Changing Standards
Discusses the role of custom in determining measured/weighed status and introduces Abu Yusuf's exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the role of custom in determining ribawi classification for non-textual items and evaluate Abu Yusuf's position that custom can override a text based on custom.

Core Idea
Custom determines the classification of items not designated by text; Abu Yusuf extends this to override old texts.

While the Hanafi school holds that textually designated items are permanently classified, many items have no explicit text. For these, local custom (urf) determines whether they are measured or weighed. The passage introduces a significant intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf argues that even where a text exists, if that text was originally based on custom, and custom has changed, the new custom should prevail. This view is not the mufta bihi but illustrates the dynamic nature of custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify items without text
List items not mentioned in the primary sources as measured or weighed. For these, custom is the determinant.
Examples: rice, nuts, honey.
2
Apply the custom rule
If people in a region buy and sell an item by weight, it is a weighed item for riba purposes; if by volume, it is measured.
Custom must be prevalent and consistent.
3
Understand Abu Yusuf's position
He argues that even for items mentioned in texts, if the text was based on prevailing custom, and custom has changed, the new custom should be followed.
This is an exception to the permanence rule.
4
Evaluate the majority view
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) maintain the permanence of textual classification, citing that the Lawgiver's ruling is not contingent on custom.
The majority view is mufta bihi.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
In a region where a textually designated item like wheat is always weighed, the majority would still require volume equality; Abu Yusuf would allow weight equality.
This affects practical fatwa.

(عيني) ما نص الشارع على أنه مكيل أو موزون، فهو كذلك أبداً، وإن ترك الناس ذلك، حتى لو باع المكيل وزناً أو الموزون كيلاً لا يجوز، وإن تساويا فيما بيعا به، حتى يعلم تساويهما بالأصالة، وما لا نص فيه تعتبر العادة، وعن أبي يوسف أن العرف على خلاف المنصوص عليه معتبر؛ لأن النص عليه في ذلك الوقت إنما كان للعادة، فكانت. المنظور إليه في ذلك الوقت، وقد تبدلت. Conditions for Valid Ribawi Exchange
States the rules for ribawi exchanges and the dispute on taqabud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for a valid ribawi exchange and explain why hand-to-hand (taqabud) is not required except in sarf.

Core Idea
In ribawi exchanges of the same genus, equality is mandatory; hand-to-hand exchange is not required — specification suffices.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq lays out the foundational conditions for selling ribawi items of the same kind. You will learn the Hanafi position on equality, the irrelevance of quality, and the critical distinction between specification (ta'yin) and hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud). Understanding these rules is essential for distinguishing valid sales from those containing riba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is exchanging ribawi items of the same genus. The ruling: valid only if equal in quantity; if varying, it is prohibited due to riba.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Umar: 'Gold for gold... except hand-to-hand.' This hadith is the basis for the inter-madhhab dispute.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Hanafis interpret 'except hand-to-hand' to mean specification (ta'yin) in the contract, not physical exchange. Thus, the hadith supports the requirement of identifying the items, not necessarily immediate delivery.
This interpretation is key to the Hanafi position.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools require hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) in food-for-food sales, citing the same hadith and the risk of a semblance of riba.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is adopted because each item is a specific sold entity, like a garment. Only in sarf (currency exchange) is physical possession required by consensus.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بجنسه متساوياً لا متفاضلاً، وجيده كرديئه، ويعتبر التعيين لا التقابض في غير الصرف أي جيد ما يجري فيه الربا

وصح بيع الحفنة بالحفنتين، والتفاحة بالتفاحتين، والبيضة بالبيضتين، .....

- وفائدة هذا أن ما يباع بالأرطال إذا بيع كيلاً بكيل غير الأواقي سواء بسواء لا يجوز؛ لأنه باع الموزون بالموزون بالكيل التي لم يقدر في الوزن، فيكون بيع الموزون بالموزون مجازفة فيبطل. (فتح) بجنسه: متعلق بقوله: "صح" أي صح بيع هذه الأشياء بجنسه حال كونه متساوياً. (عيني) لا متفاضلاً: أي لا يصح إذا كان متفاضلا؛ لوجود علة التحريم وهي التفاضل. (عيني) وجيده لقوله عليها: "جيدها ورديئها سواء" فالجودة في الأموال الربوية لا تعتبر إلا في مال اليتيم فلا يجوز للوصي بيع جيده برديء، وينبغي أن يكون الوقف كذلك، فلو باع قفيزا من حنطة جيدة بقفيزين رديئين منها لا يجوز. (فتح) ويعتبر التعيين : أي يشترط تعيين البدلين في مجلس العقد في الربويات فإن كان أحدهما ديناً والآخر عيناً، إن كان العين هو المبيع جاز، ويشترط إحضار الدين والقبض في المجلس قبل التفرق بالأبدان؛ لأن الدين لا يتعين إلا بالقبض، وإن كان الدين هو المبيع لم يجز وإن أحضره في المجلس كـ"اشتريت منك قفيز حنطة جيدة بهذا القفيز" ؛ لأنه جعل الدين مبيعاً، فصار بائعاً ما ليس عنده، وما دخل عليه الباء، فهو ثمن. لا التقابض: أي لا يشترط تقابض البدلين، حتى لو باع برا ببر بعينها، وتفرقا قبل القبض جاز، وقال الشافعي: التقابض شرط في بيع الطعام بالطعام قبل الافتراق؛ لحديث عمر بن الخطاب له: أنه عليه قال: "الذهب بالذهب رباً إلا هاء وهاء والبر بالبر رباً إلا هاء وهاء والشعير بالشعير رباً إلا هاء وهاء، والتمر بالتمر رباً إلا هاء وهاء"، ولأنه إذا لم يتقابضا في المجلس قد يتعاقب القبضان فيثبت شبهة الربا، وبه قال مالك وأحمد، ولنا أن كلاً منهما مبيع ،متعين فلا يشترط فيه القبض كثوب معين بثوب معين؛ لحصول المقصود وهو التمكن من التصرف، بخلاف الصرف؛ لأنه لا يتعين إلا بالقبض والمراد بما روي التعين غير أن ما يتعين به يختلف، فالنقدان يتعينان بالقبض، ولهذا يشترط التقابض في الصرف بالإجماع وغيرهما بالتعيين. (عيني، فتح) غير الصرف لأن التقابض فيه شرط بالإجماع. (مسكين) الحفنة: [بفتح المهملة وسكون الفاء ملأ الكفين كما في الصحاح، وفي القاموس والنهاية": ملأ الكف. (فتح)] لأنها لا تدخل تحت المعيار، فلم توجد العلة خلافاً للثلاثة، وقال صاحب "الهداية": وما دون نصف الصاع فهو في حكم الحفنة؛ لأنه لم يرد التقدير في الشرع بما دون نصف الصاع، وجاز التقدير بنصف صاع في صدقة الفطر، وروى المعلى عن محمد: أنه يكره التمرة بالتمرتين وقال كل شيء حرم في الكثير فالقليل منه حرام، وهذا هو الصحيح لصيانة أموال الناس؛ إذ عدم التقدير في الشرع بما دون نصف الصاع لا يستلزم إهدار التفاوت، لاسيما إذا اتخذ الحفنة بالحفنتين وسيلة إلى بيع نحو الكر بالكرين. (عيني، فتح)

بيع
With its genus, equal, not varying; its good is like its inferior; and specification (ta'yin) is considered, not hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) except in sarf (currency exchange) – i.e., the good in what involves riba. And the sale of a handful for two handfuls, an apple for two apples, an egg for two eggs is valid. – The benefit of this is: what is sold by the ratl, if sold by volume as a measure other than uqiyas, equal for equal, it is not permissible; because he sells a weighed item for a weighed item by a volume that was not determined in weight, so it is a sale of weighed for weighed by speculation and becomes void. (Fath) 'With its genus': relates to his statement 'valid' – i.e., the sale of these things is valid with its genus while being equal. (Ayni) 'Not varying': i.e., not valid if varying, due to the existence of the cause of prohibition, which is variation. (Ayni) 'And its good' due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Its good and its inferior are equal.' So quality in ribawi properties is not considered except in the property of an orphan – so it is not permissible for a guardian to sell good for inferior; and the same should apply to a waqf. If one sells a qafiz of good wheat for two qafizes of inferior wheat of the same type, it is not permissible. (Fath) 'And specification is considered': i.e., specification of the two counterparts in the session of contract in ribawi transactions is required. If one is a debt and the other is a specific item, if the specific item is the sold item, it is permissible, and it is required to bring the debt and take possession in the session before separation by bodies; because the debt is only specified by possession. If the debt is the sold item, it is not permissible even if he brings it in the session, like 'I bought from you a qafiz of good wheat for this qafiz' – because he made the debt a sold item, so he becomes a seller of what he does not possess, and what enters upon it with the ba' is the price. 'Not hand-to-hand exchange': i.e., hand-to-hand exchange of the two counterparts is not required, so if one sells wheat for specific wheat and they separate before taking possession, it is permissible. Al-Shafi'i said: hand-to-hand exchange is a condition in the sale of food for food before separation, due to the hadith of Umar ibn al-Khattab: the Prophet said, 'Gold for gold is riba unless hand-to-hand; wheat for wheat is riba unless hand-to-hand; barley for barley is riba unless hand-to-hand; dates for dates is riba unless hand-to-hand.' And because if they do not exchange hands in the session, the two possessions may follow each other, establishing a semblance of riba. This was also said by Malik and Ahmad. Our evidence: each of them is a specific sold item, so hand-to-hand exchange is not required, like a specific garment for a specific garment, because the object is achieved: the ability to dispose. Unlike sarf, because it is only specified by possession. And the meaning of what is narrated is specification, but that by which something is specified differs; the two currencies are specified by possession, hence hand-to-hand is required in sarf by consensus, while other items are specified by (contractual) specification. (Ayni, Fath) 'Except sarf', because hand-to-hand is a condition in it by consensus. (Miskeen) Al-hufna: with fatha on the ha and sukun on the fa, a handful, as in al-Sihah and al-Qamoos and al-Nihayah. Because it does not fall under the standard, so the cause is not found, contrary to the three (other imams). The author of al-Hidayah said: everything less than half a sa' is in the ruling of a handful, because no legal estimation has come for less than half a sa', and estimation has been allowed for half a sa' in sadaqat al-fitr. Al-Ma'alla narrated from Muhammad: he dislikes one date for two dates, and said: every ruling that is prohibited in large quantity, a small quantity of it is also prohibited, and this is correct for preserving people's property; because the lack of estimation in the Shariah for less than half a sa' does not necessitate ignoring the disparity, especially if taking a handful for two handfuls is used as a means to sell something like a kurr for two kurrs. (Ayni, Fath) Sale.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage covers the conditions for the valid exchange of ribawi items. It states that when exchanging items of the same genus, they must be equal in quantity (not varying), and quality does not matter – good and inferior are equivalent. However, this equality is not required in the case of an orphan's property or a waqf, where the guardian must not exchange good for inferior. The passage then discusses the requirement of specification: the exact items must be specified in the contract session. If one item is a debt, it must be taken possession of in the session. Regarding hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud), the Hanafi position is that it is not required for ribawi items except in currency exchange (sarf), because each item is a specific entity. The Shafi'i school, based on a hadith, requires hand-to-hand exchange in food-for-food sales to avoid the semblance of riba. The Hanafi response distinguishes between items that are specified by possession (like currency) and those specified by contract (like specific goods). Finally, the passage addresses the sale of handfuls: selling a handful of grain for two handfuls of the same is valid because a handful is not a standard measure, so the cause of riba (standard measure or weight) is absent. The author of al-Hidayah states that anything less than half a sa' is treated as a handful. There is a narration from Muhammad that he disapproves of one date for two, considering that the prohibition on large quantities extends to small quantities as a precaution.

Key Terms
التعيين (al-taʿyīn): Specification of the exact items being exchanged in the contract session.
التقابض (al-taqābuḍ): Hand-to-hand exchange of the two counterparts in the contract session.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required in a sale of wheat for wheat of the same type?
A) Equality in quantity and hand-to-hand exchange
B) Equality in quantity and specification in the contract
C) Only hand-to-hand exchange
D) Only specification in the contract

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, ribawi exchanges of the same genus require equality in quantity and specification of the items; hand-to-hand exchange is not required except in currency exchange.

The Handful Case: When Equality is Not Required
States the ruling on handfuls and the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the handful rule to determine when a sale of ribawi items with excess is valid and evaluate the intra-Hanafi difference on this issue.

Core Idea
A handful is not a standard measure, so selling one handful for two is valid; items less than half a sa' share this ruling.

This passage addresses a key exception to the riba rules: exchanging items by handfuls. Since a handful is not a standardized weight or volume, the cause of riba (standard measure) is absent, making such exchanges permissible even with inequality. However, there is an intra-Hanafi debate about the scope of this exception, and the three other imams reject it entirely. Understanding this nuance helps you apply riba rules correctly in non-standard transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for handfuls
The matn states: 'The sale of a handful for two handfuls, an apple for two apples, an egg for two eggs is valid.' This is the general rule.
2
Understand the rationale
A handful does not fall under a standard measure (like sa' or ratl). Therefore, the cause of riba (tafadul with standard measure) is absent, and the sale is permissible.
The commentary explains: 'because it does not fall under the standard, so the cause is not found.'
3
Identify the boundary set by the Hidayah
The author of al-Hidayah states: everything less than half a sa' is in the ruling of a handful, because no legal estimation has come for less than half a sa'.
This boundary is derived from the fact that half a sa' is used in sadaqat al-fitr.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Muhammad ibn al-Hasan disapproves of selling one date for two, arguing that 'anything prohibited in large quantity, a small quantity of it is also prohibited.' This is a cautionary view.
5
Contrast with the three other imams
The Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools do not permit any excess in ribawi items, regardless of whether a standard measure is used. They reject the handful exception entirely.
The commentary says: 'contrary to the three.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بجنسه متساوياً لا متفاضلاً، وجيده كرديئه، ويعتبر التعيين لا التقابض في غير الصرف أي جيد ما يجري فيه الربا

وصح بيع الحفنة بالحفنتين، والتفاحة بالتفاحتين، والبيضة بالبيضتين، .....

- وفائدة هذا أن ما يباع بالأرطال إذا بيع كيلاً بكيل غير الأواقي سواء بسواء لا يجوز؛ لأنه باع الموزون بالموزون بالكيل التي لم يقدر في الوزن، فيكون بيع الموزون بالموزون مجازفة فيبطل. (فتح) بجنسه: متعلق بقوله: "صح" أي صح بيع هذه الأشياء بجنسه حال كونه متساوياً. (عيني) لا متفاضلاً: أي لا يصح إذا كان متفاضلا؛ لوجود علة التحريم وهي التفاضل. (عيني) وجيده لقوله عليها: "جيدها ورديئها سواء" فالجودة في الأموال الربوية لا تعتبر إلا في مال اليتيم فلا يجوز للوصي بيع جيده برديء، وينبغي أن يكون الوقف كذلك، فلو باع قفيزا من حنطة جيدة بقفيزين رديئين منها لا يجوز. (فتح) ويعتبر التعيين : أي يشترط تعيين البدلين في مجلس العقد في الربويات فإن كان أحدهما ديناً والآخر عيناً، إن كان العين هو المبيع جاز، ويشترط إحضار الدين والقبض في المجلس قبل التفرق بالأبدان؛ لأن الدين لا يتعين إلا بالقبض، وإن كان الدين هو المبيع لم يجز وإن أحضره في المجلس كـ"اشتريت منك قفيز حنطة جيدة بهذا القفيز" ؛ لأنه جعل الدين مبيعاً، فصار بائعاً ما ليس عنده، وما دخل عليه الباء، فهو ثمن. لا التقابض: أي لا يشترط تقابض البدلين، حتى لو باع برا ببر بعينها، وتفرقا قبل القبض جاز، وقال الشافعي: التقابض شرط في بيع الطعام بالطعام قبل الافتراق؛ لحديث عمر بن الخطاب له: أنه عليه قال: "الذهب بالذهب رباً إلا هاء وهاء والبر بالبر رباً إلا هاء وهاء والشعير بالشعير رباً إلا هاء وهاء، والتمر بالتمر رباً إلا هاء وهاء"، ولأنه إذا لم يتقابضا في المجلس قد يتعاقب القبضان فيثبت شبهة الربا، وبه قال مالك وأحمد، ولنا أن كلاً منهما مبيع ،متعين فلا يشترط فيه القبض كثوب معين بثوب معين؛ لحصول المقصود وهو التمكن من التصرف، بخلاف الصرف؛ لأنه لا يتعين إلا بالقبض والمراد بما روي التعين غير أن ما يتعين به يختلف، فالنقدان يتعينان بالقبض، ولهذا يشترط التقابض في الصرف بالإجماع وغيرهما بالتعيين. (عيني، فتح) غير الصرف لأن التقابض فيه شرط بالإجماع. (مسكين) الحفنة: [بفتح المهملة وسكون الفاء ملأ الكفين كما في الصحاح، وفي القاموس والنهاية": ملأ الكف. (فتح)] لأنها لا تدخل تحت المعيار، فلم توجد العلة خلافاً للثلاثة، وقال صاحب "الهداية": وما دون نصف الصاع فهو في حكم الحفنة؛ لأنه لم يرد التقدير في الشرع بما دون نصف الصاع، وجاز التقدير بنصف صاع في صدقة الفطر، وروى المعلى عن محمد: أنه يكره التمرة بالتمرتين وقال كل شيء حرم في الكثير فالقليل منه حرام، وهذا هو الصحيح لصيانة أموال الناس؛ إذ عدم التقدير في الشرع بما دون نصف الصاع لا يستلزم إهدار التفاوت، لاسيما إذا اتخذ الحفنة بالحفنتين وسيلة إلى بيع نحو الكر بالكرين. (عيني، فتح)

بيع
With its genus, equal, not varying; its good is like its inferior; and specification (ta'yin) is considered, not hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) except in sarf (currency exchange) – i.e., the good in what involves riba. And the sale of a handful for two handfuls, an apple for two apples, an egg for two eggs is valid. – The benefit of this is: what is sold by the ratl, if sold by volume as a measure other than uqiyas, equal for equal, it is not permissible; because he sells a weighed item for a weighed item by a volume that was not determined in weight, so it is a sale of weighed for weighed by speculation and becomes void. (Fath) 'With its genus': relates to his statement 'valid' – i.e., the sale of these things is valid with its genus while being equal. (Ayni) 'Not varying': i.e., not valid if varying, due to the existence of the cause of prohibition, which is variation. (Ayni) 'And its good' due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Its good and its inferior are equal.' So quality in ribawi properties is not considered except in the property of an orphan – so it is not permissible for a guardian to sell good for inferior; and the same should apply to a waqf. If one sells a qafiz of good wheat for two qafizes of inferior wheat of the same type, it is not permissible. (Fath) 'And specification is considered': i.e., specification of the two counterparts in the session of contract in ribawi transactions is required. If one is a debt and the other is a specific item, if the specific item is the sold item, it is permissible, and it is required to bring the debt and take possession in the session before separation by bodies; because the debt is only specified by possession. If the debt is the sold item, it is not permissible even if he brings it in the session, like 'I bought from you a qafiz of good wheat for this qafiz' – because he made the debt a sold item, so he becomes a seller of what he does not possess, and what enters upon it with the ba' is the price. 'Not hand-to-hand exchange': i.e., hand-to-hand exchange of the two counterparts is not required, so if one sells wheat for specific wheat and they separate before taking possession, it is permissible. Al-Shafi'i said: hand-to-hand exchange is a condition in the sale of food for food before separation, due to the hadith of Umar ibn al-Khattab: the Prophet said, 'Gold for gold is riba unless hand-to-hand; wheat for wheat is riba unless hand-to-hand; barley for barley is riba unless hand-to-hand; dates for dates is riba unless hand-to-hand.' And because if they do not exchange hands in the session, the two possessions may follow each other, establishing a semblance of riba. This was also said by Malik and Ahmad. Our evidence: each of them is a specific sold item, so hand-to-hand exchange is not required, like a specific garment for a specific garment, because the object is achieved: the ability to dispose. Unlike sarf, because it is only specified by possession. And the meaning of what is narrated is specification, but that by which something is specified differs; the two currencies are specified by possession, hence hand-to-hand is required in sarf by consensus, while other items are specified by (contractual) specification. (Ayni, Fath) 'Except sarf', because hand-to-hand is a condition in it by consensus. (Miskeen) Al-hufna: with fatha on the ha and sukun on the fa, a handful, as in al-Sihah and al-Qamoos and al-Nihayah. Because it does not fall under the standard, so the cause is not found, contrary to the three (other imams). The author of al-Hidayah said: everything less than half a sa' is in the ruling of a handful, because no legal estimation has come for less than half a sa', and estimation has been allowed for half a sa' in sadaqat al-fitr. Al-Ma'alla narrated from Muhammad: he dislikes one date for two dates, and said: every ruling that is prohibited in large quantity, a small quantity of it is also prohibited, and this is correct for preserving people's property; because the lack of estimation in the Shariah for less than half a sa' does not necessitate ignoring the disparity, especially if taking a handful for two handfuls is used as a means to sell something like a kurr for two kurrs. (Ayni, Fath) Sale.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage covers the conditions for the valid exchange of ribawi items. It states that when exchanging items of the same genus, they must be equal in quantity (not varying), and quality does not matter – good and inferior are equivalent. However, this equality is not required in the case of an orphan's property or a waqf, where the guardian must not exchange good for inferior. The passage then discusses the requirement of specification: the exact items must be specified in the contract session. If one item is a debt, it must be taken possession of in the session. Regarding hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud), the Hanafi position is that it is not required for ribawi items except in currency exchange (sarf), because each item is a specific entity. The Shafi'i school, based on a hadith, requires hand-to-hand exchange in food-for-food sales to avoid the semblance of riba. The Hanafi response distinguishes between items that are specified by possession (like currency) and those specified by contract (like specific goods). Finally, the passage addresses the sale of handfuls: selling a handful of grain for two handfuls of the same is valid because a handful is not a standard measure, so the cause of riba (standard measure or weight) is absent. The author of al-Hidayah states that anything less than half a sa' is treated as a handful. There is a narration from Muhammad that he disapproves of one date for two, considering that the prohibition on large quantities extends to small quantities as a precaution.

Key Terms
الحفنة (al-ḥufna): A handful; not a standard measure, so not subject to riba rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on selling 0.4 sa' of wheat for 0.8 sa' of the same wheat?
A) Invalid because the excess is riba
B) Valid because both are less than half a sa'
C) Valid only if hand-to-hand
D) Invalid according to all schools

Key Takeaway
Items exchanged by handful (or less than half a sa') are not subject to riba rules because the cause of riba (standard measure) is absent, though caution is advised to prevent abuse.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
8 min
Conditions for a Valid Ribawi Sale: Equality, Specification, and the Taqabud Dispute
Lays out conditions for validity of ribawi sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid ribawi sale according to the Hanafi school and distinguish the Hanafi position on taqabud from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A ribawi sale requires equality in measure and specification of items, but not physical possession — except in currency exchange.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa’iq lays down the fundamental conditions for the validity of ribawi sales. These conditions ensure the prohibition of riba is avoided. The central point of ikhtilaf is whether the parties must physically exchange the goods before leaving the contract session. The Hanafi school holds that mere specification (ta'yin) is sufficient for most ribawi items, unlike the Shafi‘i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools which require mutual possession (taqabud). This lesson unpacks each condition and the proof for the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genus and equality requirement
The sale must be of the same genus (jins) and equal in measure. Disparity (tafadul) invalidates the sale because it triggers the prohibition’s cause.
E.g., wheat for wheat must be equal in volume; if one is more, it is riba.
2
Understand the quality rule
Quality is irrelevant for riba purposes: good and bad are legally equivalent. The exception is an orphan’s property or a waqf, where a guardian cannot trade good for bad.
The hadith: 'Its good and its bad are equal.'
3
Analyze the specification (ta'yin) condition
Both countervalues must be specifically identified in the contract session. If one is a debt, special rules apply: the debt must be present and possession taken before parting.
If the debt is the sold good, the sale is invalid (selling what one does not have).
4
Examine the dispute over taqabud
Hanafi: taqabud is not required for ribawi sales other than sarf. Shafi‘i (and others) require it for food-for-food sales, citing the hadith '...unless hand to hand.'
The Hanafi response interprets 'hand to hand' as specification, not possession.
5
Apply the Hanafi qiyas
Each item is a specified commodity like a garment sold for a garment; possession is only needed to specify debts and currencies, not for validity.
Sarf (currency exchange) is an exception by consensus.

Source Text

بجنسه متساوياً لا متفاضلاً، وجيده كرديئه، ويعتبر التعيين لا التقابض في غير الصرف. (فتح) بجنسه: متعلق بقوله: "صح" أي صح بيع هذه الأشياء بجنسه حال كونه متساوياً. (عيني) لا متفاضلاً: أي لا يصح إذا كان متفاضلا؛ لوجود علة التحريم وهي التفاضل. (عيني) وجيده لقوله عليها: "جيدها ورديئها سواء" فالجودة في الأموال الربوية لا تعتبر إلا في مال اليتيم فلا يجوز للوصي بيع جيده برديء، وينبغي أن يكون الوقف كذلك، فلو باع قفيزا من حنطة جيدة بقفيزين رديئين منها لا يجوز. [رمز الحقائق: ٥٨/٢] (فتح) ويعتبر التعيين : أي يشترط تعيين البدلين في مجلس العقد في الربويات فإن كان أحدهما ديناً والآخر عيناً، إن كان العين هو المبيع جاز، ويشترط إحضار الدين والقبض في المجلس قبل التفرق بالأبدان؛ لأن الدين لا يتعين إلا بالقبض، وإن كان الدين هو المبيع لم يجز وإن أحضره في المجلس كـ"اشتريت منك قفيز حنطة جيدة بهذا القفيز" ؛ لأنه جعل الدين مبيعاً، فصار بائعاً ما ليس عنده، وما دخل عليه الباء، فهو ثمن. لا التقابض: أي لا يشترط تقابض البدلين، حتى لو باع برا ببر بعينها، وتفرقا قبل القبض جاز، وقال الشافعي: التقابض شرط في بيع الطعام بالطعام قبل الافتراق؛ لحديث عمر بن الخطاب له: أنه عليه قال: "الذهب بالذهب رباً إلا هاء وهاء والبر بالبر رباً إلا هاء وهاء والشعير بالشعير رباً إلا هاء وهاء، والتمر بالتمر رباً إلا هاء وهاء"، ولأنه إذا لم يتقابضا في المجلس قد يتعاقب القبضان فيثبت شبهة الربا، وبه قال مالك وأحمد، ولنا أن كلاً منهما مبيع ،متعين فلا يشترط فيه القبض كثوب معين بثوب معين؛ لحصول المقصود وهو التمكن من التصرف، بخلاف الصرف؛ لأنه لا يتعين إلا بالقبض والمراد بما روي التعين غير أن ما يتعين به يختلف، فالنقدان يتعينان بالقبض، ولهذا يشترط التقابض في الصرف بالإجماع وغيرهما بالتعيين. (عيني، فتح) غير الصرف لأن التقابض فيه شرط بالإجماع. (مسكين)
With its genus, equally and not with disparity, and its good like its bad, and specification is considered, but not mutual possession except in sarf. (Fath) 'With its genus' is attached to his statement 'valid': i.e., the sale of these things with their genus is valid while being equal. (Ayni) 'Not with disparity': i.e., it is not valid if there is disparity due to the presence of the prohibition's cause which is disparity. (Ayni) 'And its good like its bad' because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'Its good and its bad are equal.' So quality in ribawi properties is not considered except in the property of an orphan, so it is not permissible for a guardian to sell its good for its bad, and the same should apply to a waqf. So if one sells a qafiz of good wheat for two qafiz of poor wheat, it is not valid. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 58/2] (Fath) 'And specification is considered': i.e., specification of the two countervalues is required in the contract session for ribawi items. If one is a debt and the other a specific item, and the specific item is the sold good, it is valid, but it is required to bring the debt and take possession in the session before parting physically because a debt is only specified by possession. If the debt is the sold good, it is not valid even if he brings it in the session, like 'I bought from you a qafiz of good wheat for this qafiz' because he made the debt the sold good, so he became a seller of what he does not have, and what the preposition 'ba' enters upon is the price. 'Not mutual possession': i.e., mutual possession of the two countervalues is not required, so if one sells wheat for wheat by specific amount and they part before possession, it is valid. al-Shafi'i said: possession is a condition in the sale of food for food before separation due to the hadith of Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Gold for gold is riba unless hand to hand, and wheat for wheat is riba unless hand to hand, and barley for barley is riba unless hand to hand, and dates for dates is riba unless hand to hand.' And because if they do not take possession in the session, the two possessions may occur successively, thus establishing a suspicion of riba. Malik and Ahmad also said this. Our proof is that each of them is a sold item, specified, so possession is not required in it, like a specific garment for a specific garment, because the purpose (ability to dispose) is achieved. This is unlike sarf because it is not specified except by possession. The meaning of what is narrated is specification, but the means of specification differ; currencies are specified by possession, therefore mutual possession is required in sarf by consensus, and for other items by specification. (Ayni, Fath) 'Except in sarf' because mutual possession is a condition in it by consensus. (Miskeen)
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq lays down the fundamental conditions for the validity of ribawi sales (buyu' al-ribawiyyat). It begins by stating the ruling: a ribawi sale must involve the same genus (jins), must be equal in measure (mutasawiyan), and cannot have disparity (tafadul). Quality (jawdah) is irrelevant — a good quality item is legally equivalent to a bad quality item for riba purposes, except in the case of an orphan's property or an endowment (waqf), where the guardian cannot trade good for bad. Next, it explains the requirement of specification (ta'yin): both countervalues must be specifically identified in the contract session. If one is a debt and the other a specific item, the specific item must be the sold good, and the debt must be present and possession taken before parting; if the debt is the sold good, the sale is invalid. Finally, it discusses mutual possession (taqabud): unlike the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools, the Hanafi school does not require mutual possession in the contract session for ribawi items other than sarf (currency exchange). The Hanafi proof is qiyas: since each item is a specified commodity (like a garment for a garment), the parties can part without possession and the sale is still valid; possession is only needed to specify debts and currencies. The passage includes the hadith of Umar cited by the opposing schools and the Hanafi response that this hadith refers to specification, not possession, and that the means of specification differ: for currencies it is possession, for other items it is specification itself.

Key Terms
التعيين (al-ta'yin): Specification of the two countervalues (e.g., identifying a specific heap of wheat) in the contract session.
التقابض (al-taqabud): Mutual physical taking possession of the countervalues in the contract session.
الربا (al-riba): Usury or prohibited increase in exchange of specified commodities (ribawi items).
الصرف (al-sarf): Exchange of gold for silver or silver for gold (currency exchange).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT required for a valid ribawi sale (other than sarf)?
A) Same genus
B) Equality in measure
C) Mutual possession (taqabud) in the contract session
D) Specification (ta'yin) of the countervalues

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a ribawi sale is valid if the items are of the same genus, equal in measure, and specifically identified — mutual possession is only needed for currency exchange (sarf).

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Valid Sales with Apparent Riba: Handfuls, Fruit, Fals, Meat, Cotton, and Fresh Dates
Enumeration of six valid sales with proofs and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on six specific sales that appear to involve riba, explain the reasoning for each, and identify the intra-Hanafi disputes and mufta bihi positions.

Core Idea
A handful, fruit, fals, meat, cotton cloth, and fresh dates—each valid with disparity due to absence of cause, convention, or genus difference.

The Hanafi school is renowned for its nuanced riba rulings. While same-genus ribawi items generally require equality, certain transactions are permitted because the effective cause (illa) of riba is absent, or because items are treated differently by convention. This lesson unpacks six such sales from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, each with its own proof and internal disagreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six sales and the apparent riba issue
List each sale: handful for two, fruit for two, fals for two, meat for an animal, cloth for cotton, fresh dates for dry. Note why each might be considered riba if measured items were involved.
2
Find the Hanafi reasoning for permissibility
For handful/fruit: not standard measures. For fals: conventional commodity. For meat: different genera (weighed vs. unweighed). For cloth/cotton: different genera. For fresh dates: same genus but equality required per Abu Hanifa.
3
Note intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab disputes
For fals: Muhammad opposes. For meat: Muhammad & Shafi'i oppose. For cotton/yarn: Abu Yusuf opposes Muhammad. For fresh dates: Sahibayn & three imams oppose Abu Hanifa.
4
Understand the proofs and responses
For fresh dates: the key hadith and the debate over the 'decrease' hadith. For fals: thaman vs. commodity argument. For meat: weighed vs. unweighed distinction.
5
Determine the mufta bihi for each
For fals: two shaykhs. For meat: two shaykhs. For cotton/yarn: Muhammad's view is more apparent. For fresh dates: Abu Hanifa's view is relied upon.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
